O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the end of the knowledge of medicine along with its contents, and I have finished it through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I would complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is completely unknown everywhere, so the science has perished and been lost, and nothing remains from it except the small descriptions in books by the ancients that hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed off and true knowledge is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I will make it live together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will come together with the forms of cautery instruments and other tools of the work along with the adjustment of their declaration and preparation as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good masters of hands in our time, the art of medicine has been estranged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for someone who undertakes this to ascend to the science of anatomy, as Galien says, so long as he knows the justice of members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and the number of them, and their arrangement and moving and resting veins, and from where their origin is.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And therefore says Hippocrates that a name is much if it has a name, and with the work it is little.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and all the more so in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you in the introduction to this book that whoever is not aware of the things previously said should beware lest they err and injure men.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	in such a way that I have often seen many of those who meddle with this science and abandon their own knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	I saw a foolish surgeon who cut out an abscess from the neck of a woman, and cut into her arteries.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	for which so much blood came out that the woman fell dead between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone from a man's bladder, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	so he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man inside died in three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the state of the sick person and the size of the ulcer, and I knew that if they were to cut it out, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another surgeon who took care of a duke of our land who had his leg broken and with the breakage was wounded;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the surgeon, full of ignorance, bound the break above the wound with tight stitches and did not let the wound have any dressing at all, and thus left it to its end;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commanded that he not untie it.
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and remains so until the leg is completely bloated and swelled, and comes to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I am called to come to him, and I hurry to come to loosen the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I had loosened it so, it was set at ease and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the corruption of the member was already confirmed, and I could not heal it;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease to go through the member until the entire member was completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another physician who drained a suppurating abscess, and then inflamed it further through the wickedness of his treatment.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For an ulcer, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it does not seem fitting that one touch it with iron unless it is in such a place where one can entirely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work in which there is danger in many situations;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show you in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Why it is necessary to keep yourself informed, so that foolish men may not speak badly of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your arms in custody, and treat your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that through the grace of God you may come to salvation and be praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the frightful diseases to severe treatment;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and take your arms from what causes you to doubt, and have courage in yourself so that you may come into this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galien says in some of his warnings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not undertake a sick person that you are called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have written this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are of fire cauterizations and of hot medicinal cauterizations, and the chapter is ordered from head to feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of the forms of instruments, and of the cauterizing irons, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and venesections and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and it contains the chapters ordered and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it contains the chapters ordered from head to foot, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So that we remember the work, it is necessary for me to tell the quality of the help and the harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the quality of healing and its harm is the longest and most subtle speech and the secret responses.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and many wise people spoke of this and agreed with it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and they shortened their words because I drew out the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that the fire cautery helps universally to all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions.
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to say hot complexion with matter, and dry complexion with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry complexion together with matter, no one disagreed and said that cautery there is a great aid;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is of no value for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to cure a hot disease with heat or dryness.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and he who said the opposite says that cautery makes great aid for hot and dry diseases that come into the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man to its moisture in the constitution of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true at times through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any case, do not interfere with it unless you are a doctor who has tried it, and who knows through long experience the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the cures and the timing of the time.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	we are not at all afraid of other conditions, especially in cold and damp illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors gathered together and agreed on cauterizing.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cauterizing with fire is a secret of the cure, and of greater goodness than cauterizing with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not harm except the member that is burned, and it does not hurt another member if you know its name.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The hot medicines come from member to another by dislocating, and bring great sickness of difficult healing to the affected member.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and it is likely that the patient will die.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire because of its height and the goodness of its substance does not do this, if there is no excessiveness.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And I have found this by experimentation and the great length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it was established on the truth of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this reason I excuse myself for the length of the discourse, because it does not please me that I take away from you the secret which is revealed by fire and the quality of the work, how it drives out diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	You receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time the cauterizations should be done, and appointed assistants.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is advisable at all times, because the hurtful things beneath are put right with the help of the cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and in the same way if the cauterizations are for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait for the time when greater mischief comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear son, as foolish people do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the illness that is cured by cauterization does not have a return.
et il le dient ensi;	and they say so.
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they think, because cauterization is not just a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humors that are cause of the pain, and is worth more than other medicines for its haste, and the virtue of its work and its power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And a possible thing is that the disease comes at some time according to the temperament of the patient and the location of the disease and its nature.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and the excesses are gathered in him by acquiring meat and similar things; if there aren't cauterizing administered to the place where there is a lot of excess and moisture, as with fire cauterization for pain, and similar things, and this pain does not come back.
mais ce avient poc.	but it happens often.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and that's true.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterization is worth after medicine, but their intention is false, and cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer ways of treatment in any disease and they are not worth it, then we administer cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clearly seen that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The old ones said that cauteries made with instruments of gold are more deadly than those made with iron; and they do not say this only because of the quality of gold and its high substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the place of the cautery does not become infected, but it is not true for I have tested it and found that it is true in certain men;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and gold cauteries are worth more than iron ones, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And nonetheless when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it quickly cools down;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much;
si font au feu;	they are reduced to ash.
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use iron cauterizations because they have been made more convenient to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have ordered this chapter from the head to the foot so that the view is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The oil cautery.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauteries are used for moist and cold on the brain, and there are two which are done because of an illness called "soda", and due to many humors that descend from the head towards themselves, and towards the ears, and for a multitude of dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and similarly to all illnesses that come from coldness such as paralysis and dropsy and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The shape of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a medicinal solution cleansing the head thrice or four times, according to what the virtues and the nature and the custom of the patient can endure;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make him rinse his head with water.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands on the ground.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	put the heel of your palm against the heel of his neck between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and let it bleed for a while if it needs to, then heat the cauterizing iron called "olivare", which is in this shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the marked spot with ink, and pull down and outward with your hand in a small, gentle motion.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand gently, and return the place if you see the bone as a small island.
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, then repeat the cauterizing until you see the bone just as I have told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	afterwards take a small piece of linen, and soak it in soft cotton within, and put it on the place, and let it be for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After apply a moist cloth soaked in broth on it;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and let it stay until the blister is removed.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmacium" until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And they said the old ones that when a wound is left open longer, it becomes purer.
et por ce si aide mues.	and on this account, we aid it with movement.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And one of them said that the cautery should be left in place until part of the bone is charred, and then remove what has been burned off from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And they say the other that one must let it cool on a cautery so long, and press so hard that you lower from the bone as wide as the thread that women put in their purses so that the humors may flow out.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound open for a long time.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	after that one must cure and sew it up.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two manners of cauterizing do not seem to me in any way good at all, except that in some men there is a means of fear.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	And it seems to me that I must leave it.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the shoulder is weakened by continuous flow of nature, as we witness in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and likewise when the patient's shoulder is weakened by nature, and the first appearance of a cauterization is more safe and better for me, and that I work with then seems to be salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	It seems we've reached the end of the text! The final phrase "de l'anciainne dolor du chief" can be translated to "from the old man's headache" or more literally, "from the ancient pain of the head". It appears to be a concluding remark or a note on the topic of cauterization, possibly written in an older style or from a historical perspective.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When there comes chronic pain in the head, and it lasts long, then the patient should use herbs and pills which are called "cochie", and purging of the head and oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one does to him the cauterization that we have said before, and it doesn't help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Be aware if the patient's shoulder is of strong constitution, and not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize beneath that first cauterization a little of what we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After make a fire cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make a fire cautery at the place which is called "vasselz";
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is the place where one sets poultices;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and hold your hand so that you do not see up to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and the cauterization of the horns must be finer than that of the middle part of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	from the head's cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When in one part of the head sudden pain comes and the disease is spread up to the eye and the head is purged by gentle medicines, and all other treatments that I have said in the division of diseases are done, and yet none of it helps;
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Then he makes cauterizations by two methods, namely of medicinal water and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cauterizations of medicinal water are that you take a sweet almond and remove the skin and crush it into two pieces, and then make an incision in the spot where the pain is located in such a way that you can place the crushed almond under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it has been placed, tie and hold it firmly and leave it thus for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then untie and treat the area with a poultice of garlic, and let the wound stay thus two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put on a linen cloth dipped in butter until it melts into it.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the dressing of ointment until they are healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that do the remedies concocting which I have written or in the treatment of concocted medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery so does according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery with which it is the shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "clavus" because the head is made in the shape of a nail or it has a little bit of curvature, and in the middle there is a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and gently turn the iron a little bit until the middle of the sore is burned.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift up your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and an abundance of blood pours out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Then put cotton in the space of a sheet, and place it on the spot for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then I put wetted cotton in butter, and then treat the spot with ointment until it is healed.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery that is called "culture", all along the tip, and beware of covering the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	the headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the fires mentioned above from medicine and iron do not work for him, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and then mark on the tender spot a line of half an inch in length, and take your hand away once, and hold so that you do not cover the artery and come just up to the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and be wary of the jaw that moves when it is eaten, and the nerves have regard only for the mouth and spasms do not come to the patient, and be wary also of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or cutting causes great fear and likewise for him who does not know it, and is not expert.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and let the operation continue in my way;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop blood when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it occurs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the illness, and the patient suffers, then cauterize in front of the head as we have said, and heal the wound until it is healed;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see fit, administer the cautery which we have said in the chapter of extracting the artery, with a cautery having two knives;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this is better and more helpful than that one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Of the pain of the ears due to coldness.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear due to coldness, and one has worked with dissolving medicines and other treatments that we have said in the division, and the pains do not move, then warm this spot called "point", which is its shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After that, prick all around the diseased ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and push out a little piece above the root of the ear after you have marked the place for incising.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and have x points around each ear.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treatment keep it until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torture of the mouth.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	tumors that must be treated by cauterization are none other than those that move with blood flow, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and not make a cauterization on similar things that come from scabies and eczema of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this similarity of tumor which moves with bloody flux from the eyes and purgations of head and gargling, and it is not effective, then it must be that you cauterize the patient with three cauters.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one in the root of the ear and the other a little above the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and put the cauterizer in the part that appears healthy, and make a cauterization near the top of the ear on the head above a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as one finger.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and let the cautery remain as high as half of a quern (grain-grinding stone) is burnt.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is like the cauterizing tool that we have placed before, but it is slightly more subtle and it must be that the knife is a little larger.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the cure apply the bandage as I said before, until they are healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When a patient has apoplexy and you treat them in the way we have said, and they do not recover, and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauterizations:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	two above the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one on the place which is called "vasselz" as we said before, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and let them be treated just as we have said before.
de litargie	De litargie.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	To this illness it is necessary to give the patient great herbs and purifying pills for the head.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	after, he loosens completely the hair from the patient's head, and places on the back of the head a plaster of mustard which is written in the treatise on plasters.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of cauterizing.
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he be healed thus, it is well;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not healed, then you do three cauterizations inside the head from top down to the collarbone, and have two large spaces between each cauterization.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat him in the same way as the others, and if you see that it is swollen, and the patient is suffering, then do one cauterization in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, attach two others on top of the two horns, and treat them until they are healed.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and it is the cauterizer called "olivar", as I have previously said.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of years and what we have previously said.
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after washing the head of the patient, then make him cauterize in the head and on each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is severe, then make four cauterizers on the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and leave it until the most of the core be burned, and lift up your hand.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after you have treated him until he is healed, and it is the cauterizer called "olivar" that we have previously said.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cauterization unless they are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first purify the brain with herbs and other remedies that we have mentioned in the section on treating severe and suffering patients with strong medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	If it is a child who cannot be quieted, then make them gargle and chew on a mixture that clarifies the brain often with good meats;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	after the king's remedy has been put into milk, and it is made into a paste according to what we have said before, and the paste is applied on the scab, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is weak and suffering, then make them receive cauterizations just as I have said to someone who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterization be olive according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, make one subtle cauterization in this way:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy the superfluities or moisture is corrupted and becomes thick phlegm, then make many cauterizations as we have said to someone who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if because of melancholy the superfluities are declining towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give them to drink something by which the brain may be purified, according to what was said before in the section on purifying the brain.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	after the king's remedy for the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	then make a bandage of flax well made, just like a circle, and put it on the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient should be crossed, and be held tightly from all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After presenting the linen, and moistening with old goat dung;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and the heat at a moderate fire, so that the skin can bear it;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after you have emptied the circle within the head and let it cool;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this for the patient each week once with another good treatment, until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize the area, make several points on the whole cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This manner of cautery moistens the brain equally;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on wetened cotton in cow dung and goose grease.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes' affliction (possibly referring to eye problems or vision issues)
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When affliction comes to the eyes first by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink that purifies the head, and removes all moisture from it; and make them sweat or take a bath several times fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After he commands to put the thing at the back of his head, and makes him burn it on the head, and makes two burns on the two temples if the descent of the humor is on both eyes together, or in one eye if it is in one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cut off all the veins and arteries that are under the scalp, and let the cauter be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of the bleeding out of blood, and if you see too much blood issuing, so stop it by that power which you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision, the cautery, how you should staunch it.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and whenever one makes a cauterization or blister under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the tear ducts (possibly referring to eye problems or vision issues related to tears)
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are ancient and accustomed and are on the veins or near the arteries that appear in the appearance of the head outside.
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and when you see that they are cold, frothy superfluities, then the fire cauterization that I said at the beginning of the eye should be applied descending to the eyes.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I cauterize on the head, and two cauterizations above the two temples, and two cauterizations or blister-burns under the two bones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	And if it requires more, then he should cauterize the affected area with a sharp instrument above the ring at a little fire.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the tear ducts from within the eyes (possibly referring to eye problems or vision issues related to tears coming from inside the eyes)
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you medicate him according to what we have said in the partition, and he does not get better, then give him to drink three nourishing broths.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after the king's head and the face, and have it cauterized with a mixture of the olive oil cautery.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauteries from the cautery that is called "clavilis" on the two rings, one a little below the eyebrows.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and be careful of the artery so you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the membrane of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	with which it is the shape:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see, then make two cauteries on the two rings as long as the rings are.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave your hand except until a third part of the parchment is burnt, according to the manner that I said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the eyelash which points the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	At times the hairs around the eyelids become converted to stingers, and prick the eye, and it is done with a cauterization according to two methods:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say of fire, or of burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cauterization, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they have grown and are even, then put hot oil on them;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	then mark on the paper of the eyes a shape that is as like as the leaf of myrtle, and be the beginning of the sign near the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then I put damp cotton in egg yolk and musk and pulverized pepper on the eye, then heat up the cauterization tool so this is its shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterizing on the face where you have marked it with a small dot many times, so that the skin is burned at that spot;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the parchment retracting and the hairs raised at the point of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then lift your hand and leave it thus for three days, then put moistened cotton in a burrow until the scab is removed;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the salve treatment until you are healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after this the hairs come back and the parchment is softened then resume the cauterizing on that very same spot, just as you did first;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are gone, then cauterize until the parchment is raised to its natural place and is even, and does not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The burning cauteries of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; then make on parchment the shape of the myrtle leaf.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and hot ashes, each a handful, and grind them together well;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and make it quickly, so that it does not cool down, then pour it onto the shape that you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and put it on the eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the patient has it in one eye only, then one must work on it in that one, and also in the other.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and place damp cotton under the eye a linen cloth wrapped around an egg;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the patient's head be in your lap and put your thumb showing above the medicine, and press the patty and the egg all the times that the patient feels the sting of the medicine, for they feel a stinging as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your thumb.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the blister has passed, then remove the scab and look to see if the paper is raised as well, just as it would be if it had been raised by the constriction of fire or an incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And if it is thus, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, then apply more medicine to the place or where the medicine has worked, until your operations are equal and your eyes are in order.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply damp cotton in a ball until the hot coals are extinguished, afterwards cleanse the place of ointment which is called "diaphenesis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to be careful with your treatment by taking great care that the medicine does not fall into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards and the hairs prick in the eye, then start the medicine again on that place which has become softened with good paper properly, just as you have done before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after they have been cured as much as possible;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and it is the shape of the leaf of the mulberry tree:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	Know that the eyes of men are diverse in largeness and smallness, and according to these be their afflictions;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and it should not be revealed to him whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of a fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary that you make it cauterize in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head in your armpit;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor leave his head.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	then put moistened cotton in an egg white or in pomegranate juice on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	after that heat the cautery which is similar:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and hold it to his head as a shape of a goose feather, together with the quill being the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	If you look, it is pricked from one end to the other, and if you look, it is also like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	But nonetheless, that which is prickled is moved for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	Afterwards press the fistula so it is open, and remove the pus, and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, then work on it, and drain outside the bowels;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	Afterwards put on the hot cauterizing iron, and hold your hand to the cauter on the part below the eyelid, so that your hands do not go mad;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cauter in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cauterization just up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then start again with the cauter once more, or if you need to, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After I put on moist cotton in a ball, and the treatment of ointment drying out so that they are healed, and if forty days have passed without being healed, then put on caustic medicine until the bone is exposed.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and the king according to what he would come in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cautery for a fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Understand a fistula, and open the place;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	after putting in the incision a subtle powder of which this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and they make to the quantity of a hazelnut;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand with the powder tightly, and do not let the patient move his hands until the hazelnut-sized plaster has run to its place;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary that on put on the patient's eye a damp cotton in a hen egg or in an owl;
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The poultice is applied to the place of the fistula, and the sinew by miraculous salve.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer a perforation to the navel, and bring the fistula back into its proper place in the navel.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	It happens very often that cracks in the lips are called "fur", and likewise in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with what we have said in divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cauterizing iron according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And he places a splint in those fissures until it comes together again perfectly.
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treatment the place of the boil is to be treated with cerate until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	an abscess of the jaw
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes to the root of the jaw or in the ear, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has become putrid and rotten and has been ulcerated and becomes a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not help at all.
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then it is necessary that you do the fire cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the boil or perforation of the fistula, hold your hand so that the iron may become cool at the source of it and in its last place.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and make him do so once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in cures, as long as he is healed;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if he is cured thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, it is necessary to discover the place and remove the corrupted bone, as you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	from toothache or tooth sensitivity
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure him with medicines and it does not work, then put the patient's head in your saliva;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after heating the cautery from which the form will come thus afterwards in this manner, as you put an iron on a tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and place the hot cautery inside quickly, and hold it so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	after lift your hand and reapply the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	after filling the patient's mouth with salty water, and then having them spit it out an hour later and bring forth foul pus.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was aching is confirmed to be healed, and the gums that were softened are restored, and the moisture that was corrupting is dried out.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache or dental pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When the toothache comes from cold, whether from hot or cold things, and medicines do not help, then there is need of cauterizing in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and a caustic made from wax and a fire cauterization.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	A caustic of wax is such that you take beeswax, and the end in a spoon made of iron or lead;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	after take some cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent needle, and moisten in boiling wax, and put it on the aching tooth quickly and hold until it cools.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and so do this often until the virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the linen and cotton are moist in cold wax, and put it on the aching tooth, and put on the hot iron until the fire comes to the gum of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cautery is made like this: take an iron or bronze dog (i.e. rod) and make it thick so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	after heating the cautery, its shape will come out like this afterwards, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	do this often, for the pain will be taken away that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fill their mouth with good butter in the excitement of this cautery, and then bring water.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery however long you want it to be, and as far as you are able.
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the shape of the rod
des scrophules	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrophulae are of cold and moist humors, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery as thick as this comes out in shape, and have two openings for the vapors to come out from the other side.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the hot cautery over the abscess once, or as often as is necessary, until it comes to a head on the abscess.
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days.
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and put moistened cotton on top in butter so that the scab is removed.
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing, apply the place with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cauterizing instrument:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the moistures overcome on the channels of the privy member, and especially when this comes from a cold temperament, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first by soluble medicines.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	afterwards make a cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to come close to the throat, and it should burn no more than a pea.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After this do another cautery at the junction of the neck to the head of the spine, and let the cautery be which is called "clavicle" of which we have shown the form before.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	I think I see a pattern here!
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all the diseases of the privy member are caused by cold moisture, and the patient does not have fever or heat, and it is a long-standing disease, then make two cauteries on the scrotum in the groin.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and the other cautery within the belly between two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cautery be which is called "clavicle" according to the form previously said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see, make a cautery by pricking on the entire cautery which is called "spike" of which the form is as follows in the disease of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the hairs grow just to XXX [i.e., thirty], or inquire around it.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the cure is done according to what has been said before, and the cautery is applied at three rashes according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because of that the cauteries are lighter, because you make three in one stroke.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the joint of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is put back in place, but it cannot stay and returns again with a small movement that happens, as we have proven, then you must correct the first dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	After that have him sit over his back and on his ribcage.
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	after lift the needle which is inside the titillate above the shoulder with your left hand.
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated within, then reheat the cautery which has two horns of double pitch; this is the form.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the needle as far as it pierces to the ribcage, and the mark of the cautery will appear together with four cauters.
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and therefore it is made a cautery with the cautery that has three horns, so that the figure of cauterisation will appear as six cauters.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery that has three horns.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And once it is applied to that one nerve for which there are eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After place the cautery on the pole (or point), beat with a thread.
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	after make the patient rest and do not move the limbs for a long time until he is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, this thing has happened to many people, then make a cautery on the thick spot of the cautery claw, or several cauterizers prick.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is reformed, and moisture has been removed, and the patient has recovered.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come into the stomach until it is drained to its complexion, and the patient has many catarrhs multiplied in him, and by the usual ways of treatment he does not benefit, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back, and stretch out his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Then make three cauterizations, two below the rib of the back as much as the size of an egg, completely burning the cautery; and one on each side in such a way that the shape of the cauterization is in three angles, and have this space between one and the other that they are not joined together when they spit pus.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and the cauterizations should be so deep that they reach the two parts of the bone, and the shape of the cauterizations should follow this form without adjustment.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery on the stomach in this shape;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and signing on the stomach in a point according to what you see is an inch;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	Then perform a cautery to the entire cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound that we have had before, as long as it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver suffers pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, so that it is greatly disturbed from its natural temperament by superfluities.
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is cured of what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him, then it is necessary that the patient be wrapped on his navel.
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and mark three cauterizations according to this shape and this form and this quantity on the liver, beyond the hypochondria, there where the ribs of a man come.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and let him have space between each cauterization the size of a thumb.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and be the cauteries as long as the body is, and do not press too tightly with your hand to the entire cauterization.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and be burned only half of the kernel, and the patient should be standing upright on his feet.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	And if he cannot, then sit him up and stretch out his legs, and lift up his arms.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if your will is so, then cauterize the cauteries with a cutlery, you being subtle and wise in the art, and be careful that you do not burn all the flesh, for you would dry up all the body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and let it not come just to boiling, for the flesh is very subtle in that place and you know it well.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When he has an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, then the patient does not feel pain too strongly;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the membrane, he feels unbearable pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And later when this cure depends on the skill of the physicians, it is necessary for the patient to be instructed above his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then indicate to him the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a ray, of which this is the shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery until the skin is burned and comes just to suppuration, until the pus is entirely gone;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment according to the treatment of abscesses as long as they are healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not necessary for any surgeon to use this cautery except him who has studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured at some time.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can boldly work, and nevertheless it seems to me that it is better for him to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	from the treatment of pleurisy (an inflammation of the lining surrounding the lungs)
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one should make several cauterizations with roots of aristolochia, and in this manner:
