pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of aristolochia long, the longest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your thumb.
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and moisten the root in oil and apply it to the fire, and do a fire cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauterizations one above and the other below in the part that is under the beard.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and two cauterizations between the fifth rib and the lowest one, declining a little behind.
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cautery in the chest, and another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulder blades, and two on both sides of the chest behind the cautery that is between the shoulder blades.
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not compress your hand, but hold it openly as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And an old doctor said that one should use a fire cautery similar to a razor, heat it and place it between the ribs, until it comes to that abscess.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	and sooth the pain goes out from without, as we have said about the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear for the patient to die now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse according to what we have said in the division of cures, and it does not benefit, then they apply three manners of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	Of which one method is that you make three cauteries, or four, in lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the liver cautery that we have said before.
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	and do not press your hand on all the cautery, and let the patient lean over his back.
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	and another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two handles, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder.
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and lift the knife which is at the mouse, or where the patient's breast comes towards his left side, and be the elevations from which you lift the knife according to the knife, according to the length of the body, and the cautery be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	After I put the two inflamed needles in so that the iron is perceived from the other side, and then draw out the cautery, and thus there will be four.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you see, that one should completely cauterize the whole cautery with three needles.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has become too prolonged, and this is better than the other treatments previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautionery is not useful for dropsy, except by the manner which is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you cure it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the mouth, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one in front of the chest.
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	and the cauteries should be well near to the spine from the iron.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	After that leave the cautery open for a long time so that it festers, and do not close up the patient's cure after the cautery.
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	and healing would speed along, and both intentions would come together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The form of the cauterization for the belly is the nail that we have shown you before.
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	and this one for the back is olive-shaped, as it was placed here before you.
de l’enfleure des piez	inflamation of the privy parts (i.e. a condition characterized by swelling in the genital area)
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical, and are full of watery yellow liquid, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the thumb and middle finger.
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and lift your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply into profundity, thus a fierce awl of citron wood will pierce it, and the cautery should be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	After that, make two cauterizations on each leg at the tip of the little finger.
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and be the long cauterization, one under the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg.
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	and leave the cauterizations uncovered for a long time without bandaging, until the liquid comes out.
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After the care of the other remedies that we have said.
de la menoison	From the chamber.
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When a belly flux comes from coldness and moisture, so that the virtues of retention and digestion which are in the stomach and intestines are abated, and cannot be cured by methods of remedies.
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	and you see the patient very suffering and of great virtue, so make a great cauterization on the stomach according to what has been said here before about the cauterization of the stomach, a cauterization that spreads.
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	and 4 small cauterizations around the mouth, very fine at all one small cauterization near, and 2 cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, then I do a cautery on the armpit, and one small cautery on each elbow, and two small cauterizers on the stomach near the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and of thick, cold, and moist corrupted humors, and are cured if as we have said in divisions, but it does not help, so make cauterizations.
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	On the spine of the back, that which is entirely covered by a thin skin layer and in trilaterating; and do a fire cautery below the lip.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and we see the face swell; then do one great fire cautery on the stomach, as it was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the cauterizing needle.
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	and let the cautery stay open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the place so much as it may be cured.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	It appears to be a medieval medical text, specifically dealing with various treatments for ailments.
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you cut into the abscess, if it warms up the cauterizing tool which seems razor-sharp, and then place it completely burning on that abscess cut.
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	and let your hand stay until the cauterizer comes to the birth of the vein, so that the blood cuts off;
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	do this once or twice, and if there is much abscess, cauterize each one as we have said;
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	after the treatments of ointments have been beneficial, until they are healed.
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	and if you apply a large fire cautery over the almond-shaped area, it will provide greater relief.
de plaie mal curee	a badly cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will tell about in its place, this comes to be such a sickness that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When any wound becomes a fistula, and is putrid and flows with foul and corrupt moisture, then you should try to probe it all the way down to its bottom, and know exactly how deep it goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heating the cautery until it seems red-hot, and inserting it into the fistula to the extent that the patient's tissue has entered, and reheat the cautery as often as is necessary, once or twice or three times, depending on the amount of need.
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	and beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	if the fistula goes into the bladder and to the intestine, beware of those places, and do not apply fire treatments except in the fatty part, and think that it is not completely purged.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	after curing the place until it is healed, and if the place is hollowed out, and the matter has been discharged for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed.
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	And if the matters are not removed, know that the place is overgrown, and the bone is corrupted at the base;
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	and thus as one of those which we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	The sickness of the kidneys.
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When a pain of cold comes to the reins and from gross windiness, and he does not take woman's temperament, then it is necessary that you make him have a cautery on the reins from one side and a cautery with a nail as we have said before;
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	and if we cautery him in middle, he will have three cauteries in a row, and it will make greater help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient holds back the urine, then you make him have a cautery on the part outward above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic hair begin, and to the right and to the left, and each cautery should be as long as the nose of a thumb;
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	and you must make the fire cautery on the back, or if you have need of it.
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	and let the cautery be shaped like a key according to the form previously said.
de la marris	of the kidneys
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the uterus is cold and moist, and does not allow conception for that reason, and the menses are corrupted and their termination is delayed;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	and when they come, it causes great pain;
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	then it is necessary to do for her three cauterizations around the belly, just as we have said of the bladder cautery, and two on the back;
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	and let the cauteries be shaped like a key, just as we have said.
de la hainche	of the groin or hip area
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When the moist and viscous humors descend to the hip bone, and because of this it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when you measure them together;
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	and the location of dislocation is found on the front side, so it is necessary that you perform a fire cautery on the patient above the bone of the loin at the similar cautery to the circle; and mark in front of the location around the bone as it turns, so that the bone be within the circle.
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	and if the cauteries are such like those which one has performed on the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if these cauteries are not present to you, then make three large cauteries on the olive and let them be as deep as all the kernels;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure it so long as it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the groin or hip area
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes to the bone of the loin and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient has been cured of what we have said in the section and the cure does not work, and the disease is old:
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	then it is necessary that you purge the patient of thick, fetid humors with foul-tasting pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere;	Afterwards, make a fire cauterization.
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the manner of the cauterization is in two ways:
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	that is to say, together burning medicines and fire cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cauterization is in many ways, one of which is such:
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	that you cauterize on the back of the buttock three triangular cauters according to this form, and I make a good depth and large, and let there be between each cauter a space the size of a thumb, and the cauters should be olive-shaped.
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	some time one makes a cauterization in the middle above the top of the buttock, wherefore there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you see, when you cauterize with a caustic at the circle that we have spoken of before in the dislocation of the hip.
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	but do it in such a manner that the circle contains the whole thigh, and all the sinews of the joint are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner in which it is done for sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip and does not reach as far as the thigh or as far as the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it comes just to the thigh and leg, then you make two cauterizations there where the patient says that the pain holds him, and one on top of the ankle four fingers deep, on the left side one pustule.
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	and let the cauterizations be knife-like, and let the sinews of the joint be burned.
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers of the foot or almost up to the knee, then he should cauterize there where he feels the pain three or four finger widths at the cauterization which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if necessary, do more than this.
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if he knows that the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, make him a fire cautery with a cauterizing knife or circle, and take good care in all your cauterizations so you do not blister him too much and burn the veins and large arteries, and that you do not cause more harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen many who have made a fire cautery on the heel of the foot, and left them so that the leg was completely swollen, and the feet also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purge from the belly by which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a fire cautery in one and in the other, in this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the sages said for the cauterization of the groin, this is how it should be done, make such an iron and let its head be as thick as a date stone or slightly less, and let it have spaces between them and let the space between one and another be the quantity of a pea.
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	and let the intervals be two parts above it, and also like pebbles, and there should be one iron hand with a good handle.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And it should be heated until it is all red and steamy, and then put on top of the wooden block of the sick haunch, and turned on the healthy side.
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and the cauterization should be done once in a burn and let it alone for 3 days;
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	and then make a poultice of butter, and leave the wound uncovered for a long time.
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the ointment treatment until he is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albucasis says that we use this cauterization for the fear of its retraction, and if it sees a poultice which is used.
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and all the same these are good cauterizations, that he can suffer, and at the place where it afflicts him.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The burning medical cautery is that you make an instrument between iron hoops in which the rim of the door descends, and it is made of brass or iron one palm long, and in height it has 2 nails, and between each the quantity of thickness of a thumb.
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	And they shall be overlaid with fire and above, and join together together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	After put the wooden spoon of the hip on the patient lying on the swine's skin side, and press your hand strongly onto the wooden spoon of the hip;
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	after put it between the two circles of hot water which is heated over the fire at one pot, and let it stay for an hour by good temper, and suffer the patient with heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For it finds a burn also like that of fire;
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	and when the burnings are passed, take up your hand with the instrument and lift the hip of soft ash, and let it be thus for three days, and put on honey until what is black from the scalding is removed.
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	and leave him for three days that the ulceration will subside;
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and this would be the last aid after the treatment of ointments so long as they are healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or down to the leg, then you must make the instrument that takes its shape according to what you have done in the hip similarly.
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	and this is the manner of hot water, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicines.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkaline and live charcoal, as much of one as of the other, and crush them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	where there is a small hole outward so that the point of a razor can enter.
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and put on top of that pot another pot well leaden, and put on top alkalis and cauls and hot water above, so long as there are two pots above the powder where you will have it well prepared in your hand.
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and let it stay so long as hot water and alkali or leaded pot liquid come down from it, then take all that water, and pour it on cauls and on alkalis just as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then it will be very sick and is to be treated with various medical treatments and cauterizations of other limbs.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For it does great harm like fire, and if it has other medicines in which one is well-cauterized with the groin thus as theriac and honey from the almond tree and wax with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment by which one man was cured of the pain in his side and sciatic vein, and greatly praised it, and says that no other treatment was done to him, and he was healed at once when this treatment was made, and he had bathed himself as it teaches here below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And say to take green verdigrease fresh and dry, and pound it well with one pouce of grease, and put on the groin and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain holds, and tie.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and let it be for three hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels heat.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter into a bath so that his body is well warmed up, and put him to bed, and the pain will go away altogether and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cauterization of such medicine, unless after the evacuation of body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the vein of sciatica is cauterized with fire from goat's hair, it brings much aid.
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and it must be done the cauterization in such a manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and grease it with old oil, and put it on the hollow between the thumb of the foot and the other which is called heel.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	Take dry thistle-fiber and soak it in fire until it is charcoal, and put it on the wool, and leave it until it is cold.
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and do it again in this manner, and do not stop doing it in this way until you think with your mind that it comes just to the navel, and that the pain is ceased.
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	and these manners of cauterization are called "cautery of thistle".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either by falling or by percussion or by too great evacuation, or by appearances of cold material spread out, none of these appearances is worth cauterizing, except for that which comes from the infestation of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is necessary after this that the patient be rid of fetid pills or others similar to them, which are placed on the back where the pain holds, three lines marked with ink, and in each line V cauteries or more according to virtue and quantity that the patient can bear.
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and the cauterization be done according to the cauterization which is called "pointing".
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you see, make three cauterizations or four at the middle navel cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Many times this disease comes in small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have narrow hips when they grow up, and pain.
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you find it in the lower spine of the back and in the appearance that comes on top of other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it curing, then cauterize at the cauterization of poins according to this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cautery shall penetrate evenly each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that, then you shall cauterize around the spine with fire cautery, at two or three lines, and the points shall be close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, let the place be soothed until it is sound according to what we have said, and be careful that you do not introduce fire cautery into a swelling which is near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When pain from joints is due to moisture that has spread to each member of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which the physician calls "podagre" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and cures by medicine cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterizing in this manner:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	make the mortar of cauters around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then let the fire cautery reach all the way to the point that one calls "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come just to the knee and to other joints, and this occurs often, then apply cauterization over each kneecap three or four times on each part, to the entire olive-shaped cautery.
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	and if you need more, then do it again, but hold your hand further away than the length of a spear's throw until the heated instrument is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knee and to the back, administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, then make small punctures around the fist two finger lengths;
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if there remains no pain you must do, then make punctures over each joint and over the hair on the hand.
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains come just to the ribs or just to the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and do good treatment of the patient and give medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make good government and purge phlegm, it will be made healthy by the aid of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the inflammation of the spleen
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a rupture comes in the groin, and the bowels descend to the thighs and this is new, then it is necessary that when you see them being cured, they should not move that day.
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and he uses things that cause him to belch up his belly, so that the devil descends from his belly;
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	after the treatment, have him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his breath until the bowel is reformed, and then reset at your shoulders, and make an incision below the furrow above the bone of the elbow, and do everything in a sign that is similar to half a circle over the body;
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then heat the cautery by which this form is made:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as he is white and emits fetid discharges.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then reset the bowels to their place;
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and the servants hold his hand so that they do not return backward;
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and well bind the thighs on the patient, and put a cushion under him and an officer above the thighs, and another above the chest who holds his hands;
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	Then put the cautery on the sign over your whole hand, and hold it straight and steady until you reach the bone; and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat it again another time until you feel it to the bone.
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and be careful that the boil does not burst when you perform the cautery;
que tu ne le brulasses;	that you do not burn it;
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and that through this the patient does not die, or come to some other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come just to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary for the children's cauterization to be subtle according to their size, and for the adults' also as large according to their size;
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after three days of treatment apply a piece of butter to the place of the cautery until the scab is removed;
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after applying other ointments for a cure, and the patient lies on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed;
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	and it is necessary that his nail-hair be left to grow long for a while, so that the boil does not burst when he will want to go to bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, he should be given a well-made bandage and wear it for forty more days.
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and have good rest, that he work little and beware of too great abundance of drinking and eating, and of excessive loud talking.
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	and when he does this instruction then is entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say after this the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the hernia of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When ulcers come on other sores and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then make a fire cauterization of the caustic amount, and burn the third part of the kernel.
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the treatment according to what we have said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients has said that one must cauterize with the caustic at three corners according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of the navel and make a line across it over the ulcer, and another one below, and with your hands on both sides fill up the whole cauterized area.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more superficial.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, either from falling or being hurt, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine does not help, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "poins", and let the cauteries be according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and virtue and location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	If he has been drained of blood from the first cauterization, it is well;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	since this is the custom, that he should be moved to the nearest member; wherefore it is necessary for you to make cauterizations until the patient is cleansed.
de meselerie	It seems like we've reached the end of a medical text written in an old language, likely Middle French or Old French.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The swellings are aided sometimes by a cautery with great help, and indeed the sickness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	Can you not see that it is being cauterized? Take note if the sickness is in its beginning and if it has been cured according to what we have said in division, and does not spread or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will stain all of the patient; then make three cauterizations on his head:
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I insert it into the head at nine o'clock, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the eyebrows;
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and two on the horns, and one behind on the occipital.
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and let your hand be there until the cauterization comes just to the bone, and so that the scabs come out from where the thick humors can issue forth.
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and apply the cautery to the mole as is before it.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the scabbing is scattered all over;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it comes out clearly, then you must make the first cauterization of those we have said over the head, and one on the nape, and six on the spine of the neck, and one great one on the shoulder blade and another beneath it, and two on each shoulder.
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the belly, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the pits of the hands.
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and be careful of the nerves that are above the heel calcanter, so as not to burn them;
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and never make a cauterization on the bone of the thumb, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that as I do more of a cautery, I make you an aid, and it brings you profit.
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as much as the body feels it, because the body is already quite corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterizations be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in manners of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterward treat with flour of wheat several times with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When a swelling comes in any member and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then make cauterizations on the member according to the size and smallness of the member.
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and let the cautery be a little entering into the depth of the flesh.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And at any time one makes a cauterization and to the hand and foot and back, at the issue of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if the swelling is cut out.
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and whatsoever does not meddle with it, if he is not aware of the members and the exits of the nerves moving in the body.
de albaras	of swellings
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed, and the cause of medicine does not help it, then cauterize it with a cautery one inch deep, according to the quantity of powdered sulfur, as long as the white scab is removed, and its color changes.
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	then the cure of flour of beans and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of calf and blood of almond, each a part.
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and mix everything together, and bind it with a bandage, and apply to the place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure for chancre by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a cancer comes at the beginning, and you see it arresting, then cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the edge of the cancer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And all the wise said that one should make a cauterization also in the middle of the ulcer;
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	and it seems to me that this is not good anyway, for I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen once.
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and a more direct thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called "circle", as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When someone has an illness called "adubelati", and it delays in healing or because of the superfluity that it makes or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has plenty of blood, or because of the cold.
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you see it hasten to die:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then burn him around with many small cauteries in prickly spots.
aprés le laisse ensi.	afterwards leave it so.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it perforate through the entire cautery, then heat the cautery with which it is made.
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the midst of that illness called "adubelati" as long as the cauters have pierced the skin, and be such cauters that the patient feels them everywhere in this manner that the course of the ulceration is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards heal him until he is perfectly cured.
li cure dou feu par fer	the treatment with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of illness is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a gangrene of the member, for it gnaws the members just as fire gnaws on dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this illness in a place where it can suffer both cauterization and fire, then heat the cauteries with nails very small and large, according to what is needed for the place where the illness is.
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	After the cautery of all parts, so that you burn out all the corruption, and none remains in it; that everything which is corrupted may be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the places that have been cauterized a poultice with oil until the scalds from fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of ointments produces pus.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after three days that a healthy scar does not form, it's good.
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if not, then repeat the cautery on those parts which remain corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this mixture is sometimes cured with medicinal water instead of fire cautery.
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but nonetheless fire cautery is a greater aid, and I have already said the cure with medicinal water in the division:
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Des pores that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often happens that on feet for a long time there grows a disease which is called "clod" according to our intention, and it is a thick growth that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the fire cautery of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say fire cautery and hot iron cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cautery is when you sharpen the cautery needle as sharp as an awl's point, and it should be made of good iron to a length that can pierce through from all sides, and have subtle edges.
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After placing all warm on top of the nail, and turning your hand completely around the nail until it comes to the temperature of the nail;
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and then let him leave it thus for three days until he begins to shed pus.
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	then he makes a poultice of wild mallows boiled with oil, and lets the poultice stay on all night, and the nails will fall and be pulled out of their roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the place with ointment applying fat until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted to the back of the body and have broken out in hands and feet, then you must bring him a cauterizing with hot water.
et est en teil maniere:	and it is in this manner:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	take a caldron of lead or iron, or a horn of vinegar, and put it on the nail and the warts, that is to say boils.
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	And place the cord on so that it encompasses everything around, then put a small amount of hot grease there; and hold your hand well and press your hand turning so that the edge of the cord comes to the root of the nail, and then find the hot grease path deep until to the root.
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and let the patient suffer a little the scalding of the hot liquid for an hour.
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	then leave him so, and it will unroot itself completely to all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do as with another, until you remove all those that are within the body, then treat them of ointments which bring forth flesh.
li cure dou trembler	I see a shift to a new topic!
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When someone shivers from cold or fever quartan or another thing, then it is necessary that you make four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine.
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and the fifth cautery in the groin, and the sixth above the stomach at the olive cautery.
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	If he lets it tremble, and hastens to the healthy parts of the disease of coldness.
des pustules puans	of blisters bursting
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear on the outside of the body blisters, or suppurating pustules, that come from thick corrupt matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	if it is necessary at first when they appear to make a fire cautery over each head of the pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a subtle fire cautery of ash from a fir tree, whose tip is grasped by the fire, or of root of Aristolochia longa, or a lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And every time the cauterization is done at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and they cannot grow from within, but the superfluities are broken up and they are healed;
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Often there are great discharges of blood from the artery which is cut to the wound that comes out in front, or from the incision of the abscess, or from the cautery on the member, and similar things;
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	And it is a very grievous thing to set straight.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And whatever happens to someone, if you hasten to put your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and press hard until the blood is quieted under your fingers, and no more blood comes out.
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	then put to fire the olive cauteries, small and large, until they are all red.
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then take I, a large or small one according to the wound and in the place where the artery is closest, and put the cautery on that vein which you hold with your fingers, and keep the cautery there until the blood is restrained.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bursts forth again when you lift your fingers from the wound, and the cautery cools down, then take another one quickly from those that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not cease to do those things one after the other until the blood is stanched.
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	and beware that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the patient.
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	And know that when the bleeding comes from an artery, one cannot hold it well closed even if the artery is great, unless it be by one of the four methods that we have said.
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not already closed, or by tight knot of thread, or by medicines placed on which have the power to stop blood.
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and let it be tied and held firmly in place.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who would remind me of the futility of stemming bleeding by tightly tying a cord or by applying hot things on top, or similar things, if they do not help at all. (Note: This seems to be a reflection on the fact that some methods mentioned earlier are not effective in stopping bleeding from an artery)
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if it happens to anyone and they do not have a needle or medicine present, then they must put their two fingers on the wound of the vein so as we have said, and press firmly until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein.
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and let him not move it but moisten with cold water often as long as the blood is frozen and thickened and stopped.
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and make inquiries ahead of those things which he will need of cauterization and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on surgical remedies.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have already spoken in the first chapter of all illness in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or hot medicine, and the occasions and causes and instruments and forms of cauterizations.
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I placed the first chapter from head to toe, and I will follow this chapter in the same way for what is found more easily to understand.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore that I begin this, you, dear child, must learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterization, and for that it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter there is often evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many types of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	if they come from those who have become so with their illness that they die easily due to the foolishness they find in their disease, and the great severity of their wickedness.
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and one must have fear of this.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And there are some who give you their opinion, and say:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	wait, I am well";
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the disease is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It is not fitting for you to consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more confidence in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not open yourself foolishly but prudently to those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can take and gain profit.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and make use of prognosis and indication in the treatments of your patients for whose salvation may be converted;
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and those who help you will bring about good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, may Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter for you in dividing it by chapters, as is before the chapter on cauterization, which I divided from top to bottom for you, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	A double basin full of water. (This phrase appears to be a heading or title in the text, possibly indicating that this section deals with surgical procedures involving water.)
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the afterbirth constricts too strongly the head of the child;
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and sometimes comes a cause which is replied to as if one knew it.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this disease occur outside of children, and in all those that I have seen death followed quickly.
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	and for this reason it seems to me that one should hasten the work in such cures.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child of whom the head was filled with water, and the head swelled each day so much that it could no longer be sustained.
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the swelling grew so much that it was dead, and this swelling is assembled under the bone above the scapula, between the nape of the neck and the bone.
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and the operations are such that if the swelling is between the nape of the neck and the bone, and the abscess is small, then you make a wide incision in the head.
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	And let them grow as long as II [the number two] are together, so that the moisture runs.
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and behold the shape of the poultice.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see the corners of the head open on each part, and the point jumps high when you press it with your hand from inside, and those things do not come back.
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	so you should cut three cuts into the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, draw out all the moisture entirely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	After, close the cuts with bandages and powders, and put wine and oil into them, and leave it thus until the fifth day.
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then loosen it, and treat the wound with liniments and salves, and let the head be strained in the same way, and give food to the patient dry meat or moist broth until the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another manner of incising is to look where the opening of the abscess, and the gathering of pus.
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for sometimes it is before [the] abscess.
aucune fois derrier;	sometimes behind.
aucune fois en destre;	sometimes on the right.
et aucune fois en senestre.	and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Cut then there where the abscess opens, and the gathering of pus, and do so according to what you have power.
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and beware that you do not cut the artery.
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and if a vein of blood flows, so that the patient dies from the lack of blood and the evacuation of moisture.

Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	The manner of extracting them is such that the patient must grow the hairs from their temples and listen to the artery which opens in the temple, for it beats well and can be easily heard except in some men who are very cold.
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is not heard, the patient should press their neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and warm up the place with hot water until the artery becomes evident.

puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	then scrape away the excess which is between the two ligatures at that same hour, and then, if you wish, apply the cutlery fire cautery up to the bone until the joints are scabbed.

por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	therefore it is of greater aid against the moisters.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Or, it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that you fill the place with old cotton and put on them well-made ligatures.

et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and what is more fragile and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the wound with this sharp cautery instrument having two parts, but the parts be well thick for to keep their heat longer.

Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are on the forehead of the furrow, and it is not benefiting from the care of medicine that is done there, and you see the face of the patient reddening, and feeling in the forehead a tremor as if with shivering.
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and since they are swollen and moist so that the hairs of the eyelids are down, and the eyelids are heated and scorched from the heat of the tears, then there is need for this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "cure contuse", and is that you make behind the patient who has this disease to shave the hairs from his forehead, then make three incisions on the forehead equally in length according to the length of the forehead.
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	And it may be one of the incisions just like I do all in the middle of the forehead while drinking wine down to the nape; and the other two on the sides above the kidneys, and beware of the incision of the arteries that are on the sides above the kidneys.
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and remove your hand from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be the length of three fingers through the joints.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and moistened it with cloths so that the blood can coagulate, then tie the compress tight in two parts this is its shape.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision which is below the temple to the second incision.
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and peel off all the skin that is between the two incisions to the very edge of the skull which is above the bone, then make another cut from the first incision to the other second one, and then pull out through this compress.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put in the first cut a tool called "cultellière", and it is very sharp on one side, and not sharp on the other; it should be in this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge of the knife towards the fatty flesh at the top, and the sharp edge towards the bone, and push it so that it comes to the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cover all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so long as the incision is continued until it appears through the skin; and then do the other part in the middle opening up until the other side.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then draw out equal amounts of blood, and express the place for the taken blood;
