puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put a patch of old linen in each opening, and spread moist cloths dipped in vinegar and oil and vinegar on top, and be sure that abscesses do not come;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day untie the bandage, and anoint with great abundance of wormseed plant, then apply the ointment basilicon with rose oil, and other remedies by which one cures wounds, until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	It seems like we've reached the end of this medieval medical text. The last phrase "dou reume des eulz" appears to be a fragment or a final instruction, possibly referring to some sort of poultice or treatment for the wound.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When anyone comes with acute catarrh as is customarily done, and you see the eyes thick and small, and weaken the sight, and the eyelids are burned.
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	And the hair swells, and there is great pain deep within the head, and the patient complains.
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Then you know by these accidents that those matters and the cautery come from many veins, and the mother of the patient knows what it is, if she does.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you instruct the patient to raise their forehead, then make a great incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one twice as long in its breadth.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin at the slit of the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision up to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move towards the mouth;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, then bleed all the blood onto a sponge, and then close between the two lips of the slit and put old cotton and linen cloths there;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then bind above with damp cloths in wine and oil, and take care to avoid hot abscesses;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is cut out, then you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow there, and then dress it with caustics that make flesh scab.
En teil maniere:	In such a manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of colophony, and make ointment.
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer it in these wounds so that pus issues from them completely.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the deafening of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that flows out of the ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or small stones, or a worm, or a piece of iron ore, or similar thing such as iron.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, such as eggs, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing thing, such as water and bile and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it appears in the ear as a stone or another kind of thing that does not join up with the ear, nor grows in the ear, put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, if it drips any drop of purple oil or sesame oil, then administer to it an extraction.
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and the patient makes a condiment to sweat, and stops the nostrils when the sweating comes, and puts around the ear pieces of cloth or wool.
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and the ear is above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Death often comes from this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, the patient should be given an extraction with subtle forceps, of which this is the shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it comes out with forceps, that's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, the patient should be given an extraction with a thin onion of small double fold;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not come out from there, make a string of lead and put the end of the string or needle into the ear hole very tightly, and stop what is around the string with soft wax so that the blood cannot enter with the string;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then pull it out strongly, because death often comes as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come out in this manner, take the glue of which birds take hold, and put in someone's instrument that is pointed for this to be done, and put a plug of cotton around;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the glue above the stone or whatever it is, and tear it away.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if she does not tear apart from all the things that we have said, then hurry to pierce the ear as soon as an abscess starts to come out and convulse.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of piercing is that you first have the patient bled from the cephalic vein, and extract blood according to its virtue, then sit the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty or dependent part.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the incision be as round as the moon, until you reach the stone, then extract it according to your power, and suck it hastily with your mouth.
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure it once he is bled.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if there is an abscess which swells, administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, then administer the spasmolytic warm poultice according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and apply an incision to that stone.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do it when you think the abscess is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces out of it;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then draw it with fine forceps and with a syringe, as we have said, so that the extraction may be gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In a bath then that drips into the ear it is necessary for the patient to use conditio ointment first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And there shall be a dressing on that very ear itself where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps over by itself, it is well.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	if not, take many needles according to the length of your thumb, hot and light, and heat them on the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put one or a perforation into the patient's ear, and take it out from the other side, and pierce with another needle on the needle that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and cease not to do this of stone on stone so long as water runs out completely, and thus it jumps out completely;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see it, take the joint, and stick one end in your ear, and place the other end on fire so long as the thickest part of the joint is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then redo the other part with other joints so long as water runs out completely, just as we have said in stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the animal, if it is of small body, such as a flea and similar things, treat as we have said in the chapter on divisions;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of great body that one can feel it, make a forceps extraction;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the most light thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms in the ears as a boil, when you do the cure such as we have said in the chapter on divisions and in treating of distillations, and the cure does not profit, then it is necessary that you look at the ear to the sun:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If there are any signs of pus, then treat with fine tweezers; and if they don't appear, take the catgut that is its form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And tie on the most fine knot in the ear according to the quantity of pain the patient suffers, then draw strongly until the thread is taut.
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, stop around the thread with cotton as I said in the stone.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not protrude further as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the expulsion of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distill your oils and medicines in the ear with all this instrument, which is its form as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And whether it is made of silver or of bronze, thin under at the small openings, and above over for distillation.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press down the distillation into the instrument of well-made bronze for this, and if you see squeeze the scraper and envelop it around the tip advantageously with cotton.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then you throw your oil or your juice, and all that you see of your medicines into the jug, and the jug be in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then put it inside the scraper with all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or come out of the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the sense of the patient becomes aware, and let the distilled potion be heated over the fire so that it can be distilled in the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and beware that she is not too cold, for the medicine would not be thus good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the deafening of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without a hole in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and the same thing happens to men through the closing of a wound or an abscess within the ear, and these obstructions come sometimes very deep in the ear, so that one cannot see them;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and at times it happens that the hole is completely blocked and the ear becomes quite dull.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which comes very deep, if one cannot see it, is a severe cleansing in many dispositions, and that which can be seen requires that you put the patient's ear to the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the whitish opacity, if the work has such a spot-shaped form;
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And it should be hard and thick in front and behind, completely flat, so that it does not damage the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the operation is on flesh or cartilage of the ear, then take hold with fine forceps and scrape lightly, until that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the stoppage is very deep in the ear, take the sharp thin razor and heat it a little over the fire, then put it into the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the operation at which the patient feels grief in the ear, perforate lightly, and be sure that you do not damage the nerves of the ear.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the perforation, and fill it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this every day until the wound is closed, or take a tent and fill it with red vinegar, and powder of vitriol dissolved.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear swelling, it is necessary that you remove the tent and put another moistened tent made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat them until they are healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding continues to come out, then dip a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and make use of other remedies that remove the bleeding from the wounds, such as treating with decoctions and distillations.
de la char des papieres	It seems like you've added a few lines from an old medical text.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	These swellings that come on the eyelids when they are moist and dry, it is necessary to spread them with tweezers and forceps, and scrape off a spatula from their roots.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then place verdigris powder on the joint.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if the scab falls off, then cauterize with a lentil-shaped cautery and the cauterizer after the incision is worth more.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and many times they repair, so that nothing remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are charred and do not return.
de la gresle	hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come on the eyelids certain things that seem frost in their shape and hardness, and because of this is called "grandine", and it is an assembly of moist substance thick on top and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	The works are thus:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Take note that the swelling moves from one side to another and this is an easy thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Make it then double in length, then scrape off from each part lightly, then take it to the pincers and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cut it without piercing a small spot of parchment, so nothing hurts the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the crack is great, then put it back together with a suture, and heal it until it is sound.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, don't apply any pressure, for the swelling will soon reduce and become flesh again.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the swelling is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then turn over the parchment and stitch the swelling with pincers, and cut and press from one side and the other;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does not harm anything;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the boil is cut open, if the eye of sea salt is applied to it, and care is taken for the place where the unhealthy flesh swells until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	meibomian gland cyst or chalazion (a type of eyelid lump)
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease that swells in the pages of paper on top, and this happens more often in children than in anyone else, and it causes them much pain, and they come to have catharrs in the mornings, and are unable to look at the light of the sun because the tears rush into their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and because of this they lie on their faces again and again, and sleep on them, and have paper under their eyelids, damp from the swelling and appearance that cover the exinach which shows in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place to your two fists and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the treatment is that the patient place their head in a scalding hot bath.
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains Esrinnach from each part, then place it on him;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your arms on one side and the other so that Esrinnach is assembled in the middle of the circle.
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make in mid-water of the wet sharp spatula a gash of a small depth, and not be any wider than the wound that one makes on the vein.
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make the skin in depth until you come to Esrinnach.
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many dispositions comes Esrinnach out of the gash, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Remove then the whole cloth of which the hem is frayed between your hands at the far end, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and keep that you do not add to the tear, that you do not reach right up to the entire spatulum just as far as the eye, that you do not cut it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the extractor does not open in the beginning of the tear, so make a small piece of the tear slight until it opens.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then remove it as we have said, then moisten cloth in oil and water, and put on the place, and remove with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such men who burn silk and put it on top to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal it until they are sound.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hot abscess comes to the place, then heal with soothing plasters until it is sound.
des poilz des papieres	of papers of wool
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When the hairs on the eyelids grow in an unnatural way and are inflamed, if they harm the eyes, and bring forth manners of illnesses such as habitual tears and softening of the eyelids and conjunctivitis, so that it is a cause of the destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and there is a treatment according to four manners:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by fire cautery altogether, or by medicated water according to the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by bandages, as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the patient's head in your own shoulder, then turn the paper of oil to your left hand.
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is turned back, that is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	but if not, then you put a needle into all the thread on top.
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and if it is along the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow near those hairs, and pull the thread upwards to all the paper, and turn it on the razor.
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make in the part under the paper, under the hairs joined together, to all the spatula cutting, from the large tear to the small.
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then draw out the thread, and put beneath the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then mark on the paper a shape of an ivy vine, like the leaf of myrtle, and in all ways it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see rise from the paper which is divided into parts.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if there is someone who needs it, one cuts out a large quantity of the paper according to what the paper is softened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then make on the entire space above the two lines that you have marked, and begin to draw a large letter "L" just up to small.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and make it one of the slits near to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then stick the thread in one of its two corners next to the skin, then scrape off all.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then sew the two lips together with a seam of a needle to all the thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and dry off the superfluity of threads above the two circles on anything that is sticky, if you see this.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, then do not treat it, but leave the stitches and threads for three days or four;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then treat the wound without stitches with drying and constricting things; for paper will adhere to the union of the wound but the stitches are rotten (as said by the ancient ones) and this is a task without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	and if there is another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you shape the paper into a figure like the leaf of myrtle, as we have shown, with three incisions split off according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take note of what rises to equal strength simultaneously according to the shape which is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you do not have the power to hold the forceps and the thing is not even, then take a needle with one thread and put it through the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and insert the other thread near the large wound, and the second thread near the small one, and bring the two threads together evenly between your fingers;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift your hand evenly, and lift the entire skin above which you have marked, just as we have recounted, then bring together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and care for it until it is healed;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with wax and similar ointments softening;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and at some time happens that the hairs of the parchment are changed:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	then it is necessary that you use what we have said about incising;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching in one and the other is more artificialized.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of canines is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you should stitch the parchment and make an incision within according to what I have said, and then make two canines by art, and two thin ligatures as long as the parchment and the width of the spatula are;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and tie up the two shoulders with two threads where you hold the sons;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then tie them together delicately above what comes out from the paper of the eye, and hold fast the two tendons in both parts together;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that was strained will die and turn black and swell, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it lingers, if the tie holds with strength, then heal it as long as it is sound;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is healed and the paper has lifted up and they can no longer be felt the hairs;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the shape of the two tendons that you will do according to this figure and according to this length and width;
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the works are such as when you take a fine needle, and you put in the thread of silk soft and fine;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	Then gather the pieces and join them together subtly, and let the length of the strings be a cubit in length.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	Then take another fine thread of silk briefly, and knot the ends of the string together.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then put the patient's head into your hand.
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be near the sun so that the work may be made clear, for this is a subtle and small operation, then insert the needle into the entire length of the skin at the root of the hair joined together, and make it pierce quickly through until you draw it up over the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then pull out the hair until it is above the skin, and insert that hair into the skin, if there are one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then pull out your hand until the hairs come forth through to the entire length of the skin in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the skin is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will pull the skin to the underside for all the thread that you have ordered there, so that the skin comes out through the opening above and you can see it by the sight of the eye.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	then you will pull the skin and the thread, close your eye and leave it closed for two days or three, so that the hair returns to its place and the scar above grows.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hairs are short, then accompany them with long hair of natural origin, and raise it along with that one until they are lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the inflammation of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the corruption comes into the eye, then it occurs in two ways:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	the natural, and the unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs through sudden injury, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of performing this operation is that you cut open that seam, and sever the lips, and put linen tents inside, and tie it so that it heals.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not necessary to use in its treatment things that dry up and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than the first one.
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but the work of things that soften it, such as fennel.
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and let the roots of aqua or aloe and flax seeds be cooked, and unguents made from dissolved diacolin in any oil, and envelop it in a tent, and treat with these things.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your treatment is that you take great care that it does not congeal in the form that it was before.
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these operations which we have said are not other than means to prevent this illness from returning in the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh (or ulcer) that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is located below, which is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from a wound and a fracture and a cautery and similar things.
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way of doing this operation is that you take a needle in which it has double thread, and insert the point into the flesh, and make it pierce from left armpit to right, so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then cut the flesh above all the needle and the cord is as wide as the thumb.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the appearance of the paper returns according to what it should be, that's good.
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, take a razor and put it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two cuts or incisions on both sides of the paper.
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and the holes of the two incisions are at the two corners of the cut that you have made, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is as the shape of a letter which has the name "Grisian".
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then take away that skin, according to the amount of its edges are worn down under, from what is shown on the parchment, then join together the two separate parts and sew them with a thread of linen.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply the treatment of those things that we have said about softening medicines and plasters, until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from an incision or a cut or a cauterization, it is necessary that you make a flat incision under the hairs of the parchment, and according to what is said before.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	Then separate between the two leaves of a plaster, as I have said.
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and the work should be done according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare remedies of all their power so that they bring back the figure to its natural shape.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what needs to be done and the tools used in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	the suddenness of paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this wound has happened in such a manner that the paper above is stuck with the white of an egg, and cannot move or do its natural workings, then it is necessary to put the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and then with the splints and forceps, as you cut off what is congealed on the fragile part, not too sharp nor too dull, so that the patient cannot bear it if the splint is too sharp and hurts the eye.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and let your incision be such that you peel off the congealed part lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural shape.
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and cleanse all the congealed part, and make no further attempts with salted water in the eye, and lift out with sweet water and vinegar.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	Then put a linen cloth between the paper and the eye; and place damp wool on the eye in abundance of egg.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and afterwards for three days use a bandage and strong bindings until they are healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	the corner of the eyelid
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail is according to two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	it is nervous and similar to the hard skin of a scab, and another which is not nervous, but is similar to white moistened congealed blood, which when touched with iron and thought to be pierced with tweezers, cannot be.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and both forms begin around the main tear duct, and grow little by little until it covers all the eye and its light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of incision is that the patient places their head under a beam, then closes their eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and take some paper to your hand, then draw an ink line with tweezers of small thickness, and stretch it upwards.
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put in a horse's hair, or a cow's hair, or a bull's hair, and a strong thread.
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and stick it in the ink line, and pierce all the way through the needle, and tie the ink line with thread and stretch it upwards, and scrape off all the hair from the side of the ink line which touches the parchment, as far as the hair reaches to the top, then cut the remaining part at the root of the hair on either side, very finely and with little force, and leave the natural flesh or skin uncut, so that through the incision the body's accustomed tears do not come.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and at no time stretch the ink line or thread alone, as we have said.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Then one has to scrape off all the scurf from the shoulder of which this is the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And take care that the shoulder does not touch the fleshy tissue and break it, and that the axillary node is not pierced;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision throw into the eye a piece of bruised flax, and a little collirium made of quicklime, and let it stay until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal him with what is necessary until he is sound.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the joint is not numb, and you cannot push in the needle, and the splints cannot enter, often this likeness of a joint is cured with medicine;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and it will heal just as I told in the section, and if you see it cover over, work on the eye of the patient, and take the shoulder skin with a light prick according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And gently rub the corner of the eye, and if you see that it does not reduce in size and the reason hastens, then spit into the eye a distillation made from lapis lazuli and with red camphor mixed together, and bandage the eye until the other day.
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then repeat the other work according to this same operation, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything is not contrary in the eye, as a hot apostema or boil, then drain it, and first cure the hot apostema until it is healed, then continue with the work just as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh from the abscess causes great harm in the eye, then suspend it with a cloth and cut off a part but not all, so that the body of pus does not come.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill red camphor into the eye, which is made from lapis lazuli.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	It seems you've changed to a new topic.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	The eyes of some men become red at times, and cover the eyelid and hold on to the papers and turn them towards the back, and seem like a pomegranate flower.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	The patient must place their head in the hot water, then they should close the eyes, and cool down all that flesh with poultices suitable to them, and hold it firmly at the strength.
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then scrape off the first skin, and go scraping all the way to the end, and be careful not to cut the eye during the operation.
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and the incision should be like a spatula that we have said in the incision of an ulcer and with little force to remove the scab, just as the form shows after this chapter demonstrates it.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is completed and all the skin is removed, then pour oil of silk or you distill red vinegar and similar corrosive medicines onto the eye, and put on top of the eye cotton with egg white, so that it be secure from a hot abscess.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	And if it remains still, and the blood does not surge forth, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the eye alone and treat the hot abscess with soothing things;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make the vein that has been cut in the eye by this condition stop.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But nonetheless it is necessary for you to ease the treatment of each weak vein of its natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and of the accidental way, in iron work;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of veins of eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	There are red spots that cover the eye, and they obstruct the work of sight and weaken the eye completely.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is necessary therefore at first to look and see if the vein in which the abscess has grown is swollen, and there is no other foreign illness except for the abscess;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then treat the vein in that manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	command the patient to place his head in hot water, then suspend those veins all around him according to his knowledge, and let the vessels be subtle and double like this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be two threads by degree in one body in this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then tie those fine veins subtly, and check the blood hour after another, until you see those veins moving out of sight.
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and take care not to prick the eye with the points of the spatula, and do this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you don't miss those veins.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, then make the green and red vinegar in the eye to corrupt what remains in the scale.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you are unable to tie all of that in one hour, make a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are soothed and you are assured of hot abscess, then start again in this manner as before until they are healed.
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of strength:
de la fistule de l’oil	It seems that the text has come to an end with "de la fistule de l'oil", which means "of the eye abscess" or "fistula of the eye". This is likely a medical term from the Middle Ages, referring to a condition where there is an abnormal connection or channel between the inside and outside of the eye.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The surgeon calls these "arissati" fistulas:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you cure it by cauterization and with a hot medicine as I have previously said, and it is not healed, then there is trickery in the place where you cut into the abscess, there where it should die, and extract all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see the corruption and blackness, then raise it with all the instrument of which this form is;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "asperge chief", and should be made of iron which is pointed at the top, and should be pointed like a file as in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your thumbs, and press your hand a bit until you know that that corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this at any time, then restore the place with medicinal cauterization.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the wound is sewn up and flesh forms there, and the body of the bow is sewn up and remains in this way for XL days, and it does not renew itself nor become an abscess, and a bad accident does not occur, know that it is healed;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	if this is not so, then there is no other cause except to bring the fistula back into the natural opening of the navel according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you uncover the bone the second time by iron and sharp medicines, and when you have uncovered it take the iron according to this form, and let the iron head be at three angles, and the fistula be thinned down just to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone near the abscess, and move your hand away from the eye I touch, then turn all of the iron as far as it will pierce the bone and the patient feels it through that which the blood flows in if he holds his hand over his navel;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	And then restore the place of dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the place, so go to the fridge;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye (i.e. the pus or fluid)
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes open widely and there is no hindrance or obstruction to the fridge, nor any diminishment, then you must bind the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then clean it, then apply leeches or ligatures near the wound to drain, then put on the eye a paste made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarsaparilla, and then strain the eye, and cover it over with bandages and cloths.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and fold each one into four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes need.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then bind it above with a sturdy bandage, and apply the cupping glasses again to suck without causing pain;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the cupping glasses and let the eye be bound tight day and night, and if it swells, you should bind it tighter;
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see that the eye is mending, it's good;
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	so restart the poultice and the cloths and the bandage and the cupping glasses until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the rupture of a transparent membrane (i.e. a detached retina)
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When there is disruption in the vitreous humour, it opens up and comes forth in little papers like grains of resin, and it is frightening to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you see it closing over, the work is such that you prick a needle into the root of the part below just up to the top, then insert another needle where there is the double thread from the part of the eyelid;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and have it pierced, and let the first needle remain according to its position;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then twist the end of the thread double and tie one part of the eye around it, and hold it tight, then pull out the needle and put a linen cloth moistened in egg white on top;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the thread becomes tangled with the eye, then heal the wound with comforting things until the pain is gone;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and at any time the wound is held in place by the eye each side of a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eyes give a great appearance, then pierce them with a fine awl which comes near the root of the eye, and clean the moistened albuculus and descend the eye, and enter immediately;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then pull it out until they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Of the lower part of the eye (i.e. the conjunctiva or the sclera).
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease called "alcunnati" is not other than the eyebrow which is assembled in the eye, resembling an icicle descending, and it is not an icicle.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of the appearance of the operation is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take their head between your hands from two parts, and move it so that you see the eyebrow coming up to your eyes.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then close your fingers, do not let it descend and cover their eyes with the light, and see the patient's things as they are accustomed.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is an icicle, and the descent of the eyebrow is not aligned as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	then make the patient sit between your hands, then take the thin spatula and insert it above the corned thread from the edge of the conjunctiva with the corned thread and the crown, so that the eyebrow comes out.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is dislocated, then it should be distilled in hot clear water mixed with honey, or in vinegar or fennel seed boiled and mixed with honey, then it should be cured by another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Of the threads (i.e. filaments) of the eye.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have seen the likenesses of waters in division, and what is needed to puncture.
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if according to the work for health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, far from the light of the sun, and bind the sound eye very tightly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or on your right hand if the eyes are right-handed.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand if the eyes are left-handed, or in your left hand if the eyes are right-handed, the instrument called "almagda".
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the point of the instrument near the crown by the thickness of a reed in that white part of the eye closest to the smaller eyelash. Then insert the instrument called "almagda" virtuously and turn your hand so it pierces the white part of the eye, and feel when almagda reaches the empty thing;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the length of the path of almagda be exactly the length of the distance from the pupil to the end of the black part;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and that is the white of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone in that paper due to the transparency of the crystalline lens, and then place the instrument just at the place where the water is, then press under one way after another;
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he has water now, so sees the patient before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After resting for a little while, and if the water rises through the second way, place the force with the instrument, and when it is firmly stuck and does not rise, then draw out almagda lightly by turning your hand slowly and slowly;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then immerse in water a small quantity of silk thread, and lift from it the eye inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put behind the eye a poultice or wet cloth in rose oil and abundance of egg white, and bind with clean linen.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We now, and those who are of our time, put on a compress with abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter into the eye by its hardness, for there are many men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument which is called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then puncture only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle point, then insert alum, as we have said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a bed suitable to him, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be free of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or to the left, and be tied according to his condition until three days.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then release him in that same dark house, and examine his eye, and make him look at some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not necessary that you do this in the work of healing or after the incision now, but rather that you speed them up, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	When an abscess appears, instruct the patient to bind the eye near it on the seventh day, and apply a poultice that soothes the abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is quieted, then unbind the eye and place a yellowish ointment on its face to cover any sore for a day, and it should be thus in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then he will leave the dark house and go about, and recover fully.
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And someone came to us who was from Hircania, who told us that in his peaceful land they did the operation of Almagd or Perceid, through which one sucks water, but nonetheless I never saw any such person in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the signs of the forms of elephantiasis, because one who does not know them will see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and they are of arsenic properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads should be the same subtle shape, and the base in three sharp points.
de la char sor le neis	from the skin above the navel
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	At times there emerge or are born various kinds of boils which resemble scorpions in the many spots;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there are such or he has a boil with fiery colour and a sore of good colour.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that then of the sores which is not fiery and not blackened, it is necessary for you to make the patient sit between your hands against the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open his nostrils, and spit on those sores, and treat them further.
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then take what you must support at the spatula with subtle point from one side, as long as you know that that sore is all open.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains any thing that cannot be cut out, then scrape away with all the subtle and light instruments, so that nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if pus does not rise up, or an abscess forms, then let it dry as is proper;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten and apply the cautery until the blood is stopped and all the ulcers are removed, then pour vinegar or else sharp wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the abscess works itself outward, and moisture comes up to the throat, know that it is healing;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not break through as is proper, know that there is raw flesh in the bone above, to which the instruments do not come to cut;
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then it is necessary that you put in a piece of linen thread not too thick, and well oiled with the hands' grease, and have between each knot a space or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient's shoulder joint into a cloth or pouch at his power, and tie it with thread so that it comes through the neck within the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times children do thus in their games, and it is an easy thing for him who wishes to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then take the head that comes through the neck in one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth in the other hand, and pull one after the other along with those which are on the thread;
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	do this as long as you know that the new joint has taken hold of that flesh, then pull on the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back into place just as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	do this for three days or more, until the salve has eaten away all that remains of flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	And then put him in a poultice of plaster for some days until he is healed; and if he needs dry medicine, so use it.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the shape of the instrument to purge the head, with which one distills oils and medicines nearby:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it should be of silver or lead, resembling an open lamp like a cauldron, and the conductor also.
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you wish, make a closed cauldron, and the instruments should be filled to purge the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and it should have two handles at the head to hold him when one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the skin above the navel
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Often a disease occurs on the head near the poultice called "telul", and it grows and becomes large at once, so much so that it is a visible thing to look at.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	And for this reason it is necessary to apply the poultice at the beginning, and then cover with new flesh the bone entirely bare, then put on its place the cauter or the burning medicament.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you delay covering it until it is large, take note if it is hard, of bad flesh color, and poor sense.
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	do not touch it with iron at all because it is an infected abscess, for whenever you cover it once, great harm comes to the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of soft touch, not bad flesh color, and you see that it can be covered entirely, then have the patient void themselves and the covering sense has no pain, and treat the place with drying and binding things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the navel is cut open and cleaned
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of the cartilaginous works, it gives little profit, worse than in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	it is therefore necessary to cleanse it in this way if it occurs at any time, so look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then join the two lips together with a suture, then heal it until they are sound.
