et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are already split from one part and the other, then you should remove all the parts of their skin so long as they heal, then join the two lips together with a suture, and bind it, and sprinkle on powder made from dragon's blood and burnt incense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on top of the powders a piece of plaster made from strong or another binding plaster, and let it alone until he is feverish by himself, then heal him with ointment so long as they are sound.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of suturing is that you assemble the stitch:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly.
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	Abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Many people have abscesses inside their lips, which are hard and resemble small pebbles or grains.
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	Then it is necessary to pull the lips apart and incise each notch, and take hold of it with tweezers and cut in each part.
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	Then apply vinegar to the place after the incision has been made, until the blood is stopped.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then apply oil of lily and treat the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	from the gum tissue
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	There are often on the gums a growth that the ancients called "albulus".
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	You should hold it with forceps and cut at its root, and let the string or blood bleed.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	Then apply vinegar to the wound, or other constricting and drying powders.
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that scar comes back after the incision, and it happens many times, then cover it again the second time, and cauterize.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not come back after the cautery.
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the shapes of the dressings to cover.
des sordens	of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they are gathered at the head of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and harsh.
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes they are black and yellowish and worm-like until the corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth stinks.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	if it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your grasp, and straighten the teeth or scabs that appear, until there remains nothing.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus make a blackening and a blanching, and a yellowishness and the other stains, until they are cleaned.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes what is attached at its first reason, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then let it relapse the second day and the third, until you have everything reset;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the teeth have need of various forms of instruments to reset them, according to what the work shows, because the raspers with which one files away from the teeth are of different forms than those with which one files between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others should be prepared by you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat the tooth for its pain that you wait until the point of extraction as long as you can, because it should not be done quickly;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because it is a very hard substance almost up to where one cannot file.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When then the patient is constrained to be drawn, it behooves you to be certain about the depth of extraction.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Often the pain would go away from the patient, and she believed it was a toothache, and had the good tooth extracted;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	And yet the pain does not part from them, as long as the bad humors are present, for we have often seen this in our lords.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are certain about the decayed tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth on all sides with a sharp spatula in order to preserve the gum from all parts.
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move it with your fingers or fine pincers to the first pull and pull, until they are well loosened, then firmly tighten the pincers.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and the head of the patient be in your sight between your knees, and keep it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and push it inside from each part lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, then you should fill it with cloths, there where the perforation are.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you pull out gently with pincers, that it does not break when being pulled out.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to carefully work around the gum for a discharge of the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and inform the patient that through the evil of the root there will be greater pains than at first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And be warned that you do not act in the manner of foolish healers who, through their hastiness and boldness, sometimes break the carriage, and bring no benefit of what we have mentioned.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but sometimes bring about a great illness through the corruption of the roots that remain, or because they break the carriage, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is loose, wash the place with vinegar or else with ass's gall and salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if the discharge of blood comes from it, which often happens, then apply a poultice to the place with vinegar.
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that does not help, burn it (with a cautery).
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of the tweezers by which one must pull out the teeth first are with long points and thick handles, that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick limbs so that they do not bend at all, and let them be iron plates well made, and let them be held by teeth to keep them in place.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in the wound, you must put moistened cotton or butter on it for one day or two, until the place is softened, then insert the pincers called "algefri", by which the bone seems to be bitten;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and those that are inside should also be done in this way as with an awl and that is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out with those pliers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", i.e., pincers, by which this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be firm and thick so that it does not break, and if the root bursts through them, it is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if not, then help yourself with all the instruments by which these forms come later:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if that doesn't help with this instrument that has two rings, by which this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other bandages that are placed in front of the teeth, and this instrument which resembles large pincers, the shape of which is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let those instruments be strong so that they cannot break, and know that many types of dens are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments which are not counted;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise and subtle masters find their instrument by themselves, according to what their work and the disease shows them, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of the limbs and if it breaks the charrette or other bones, or it does not fit, so I look for the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and help from gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And be large and well-holding to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but rather hold and remove;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the place with medicine suitable for these, and if there is putrefaction in the bone and it is small, so return to all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural body and the form is ugly, and even in virgins, it behooves that you know whether the tooth is newly after the tooth and is not in its proper place, and one cannot straighten or whet them:
adonques lou raie;	Therefore do a resetting.
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	And if it is stuck with the tooth, take this instrument whose form we show here and which resembles a small beak, and it should be of iron indented at the tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle is short and short in one's hand for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears to be able to be filed, take a file like this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and similarly to a whetstone with which we make needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and whet the tooth little by little in your hands so that it does not move until it is sharp.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then smooth the sharpness off at both ends with a file; and if the tooth is too pointed and it hurts the tongue, you must whet the roughness until it is even so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt the voice.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front tooth is knocked loose through a blow or fall, and the patient cannot press down on it so that it does not fall out, and you have treated them with binding medicines, and these are useless.
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	If they need to be held steady with a thread of gold, because the son of silver becomes green and rotten, but gold never changes.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be of moderate thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the bones.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you see the bones directed away from each other, take the thread and bind it double between the two healthy bones, then put the ends between the diseased bones, if there is one or more, until you come to a sound tooth on the other side.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then re-cover it just to the part where you began, and hold your hand subtly and steadily until it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and be sure of the ligature at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then twist the ends of the thread in pincers and join them together, and re-pull them between the sound tooth and put it so that it does not hurt the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	And then leave him thus tight as long as he can stay, and if it dislocates or the threads break, then hold it with another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if he stays and serves thus all his time, and this is the shape of teeth and the form of the arrangement of two sound teeth and two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, if it is put back in its place fresh by fresh, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and does not meddle with it unless one is wise and patient, and at any time makes the shape of a calf bone tooth, and puts it in place where the defect is, and holds it fast as we have said, and stays and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to uncover the ligature of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	At any time this thing comes from under the tongue or by nature, which one is born with;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	by accidental injury to a healed wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you should operate on the patient's mouth and have their head in your hand, and lift the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the ligament of the nerve of the tongue as far as it is loose and separate the tongue from its place, and if there is any hardness or knot, which comes from an old wound, then insert a thread and cut the ligament;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and beware that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which is below;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done this, if you can raise the swelling of a boil or carbuncle, or a cold abscess, then place a cloth of linen under the tongue;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and apply to the patient's boil each night so that it cannot consolidate.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if there is a discharge of blood, then place on the boil vitreous poultice.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the blood overflows, then bleed with the slow fire cauterization, which is good for those;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat with another treatment until they are healed;
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if the abscess was of a foul colour or black or hard, and the patient did not feel it, do not touch it, for it is an ulcer;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining towards the bladder, and there is moisture, then pour wine into it, and make a poultice from very fine linen, and deliver him from one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the blood overflows at your operation, put on vitriol powder until it is stopped, then come back to your operation as long as you draw out all the bad stuff;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the place of the armpit and of the groin, and treat with other treatments until they are healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Il semble que le texte soit une traduction ou un résumé d'une partie du "Régime du corps" attribué à Guy de Chauliac, médecin de Charles V du roi d'Arles (1347-1380).
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Throats occasionally come within the gorge called "godath", and they are properly called the "amandres"; and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful.
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it is a hardened abscess of little sense and foul colour, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is thick, also do not touch it with iron, for the bleeding of blood.
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it be until it dies, and then you will part it, lest it break by itself.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white colour and greenish, and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cut, but first see if the abscess has cooled down and is calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and your hands be pure, and open his mouth and take hold of the servants between his hands, and press the tongue underneath all the instrument, by which it is made.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it shall be of silver or subtle tin, as fine knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Can you press the tongue against all this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the thread and push it into the ember, and let it burn above as much as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and pull out anything from the threads with it, then scrape off with the instrument, of which this is the form, that seems like a force;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and nonetheless the heads are curved, and one end against the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	Je pense que j'ai compris la traduction ! Voici :
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And be cut on one side, and notched on the other;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have scraped one of the embers, if you scrape the other in the same manner, and after the incision make the patient gargle with hot water, and warm, and easy, and as soon as the blood comes out, make the patient gargle again, or peel from green apples that have been cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then the treatment continues until they are healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and at any time swellings in the throat arise like two almonds, so treat them then just as are treated the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I have medicated a woman for an abscess that was born inside her throat, namely the abscess of little sense.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had been well encircled all around the throat, so that the woman could not exhale because of the duct which was obstructed, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so high that it had forced out two pus-filled boils through the two openings of the birth canal.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened then at once, and sewed on one of the sutures, then the tumour burst out, and in it there was a large portion of pus.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I sewed up the other part on the other opening of birth, and operated on the mouth and pressed the tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After piercing the onion in these abscesses, and cutting out a part of it, and only came out that a small amount of blood;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus was the conduct of the woman's throat unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease cutting out this abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess kept growing again, and filled up the place that I had emptied, so much so that it became very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I bound it and cauterized inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	thus it stopped growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I left these parts, and was only aware that God did with them after me.
de l’uve	It seems like you're trying to translate something from an old language or text.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When swelling comes to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is under a large and rounded one, it is called "eye
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the boil has been calmed down and is subtle, then you should lance it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is round and assembled together, and is not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or of a greenish or black colour, then you should let the incision of it bleed.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger over the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, regarding its swelling and length, that you seat the patient in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we have mentioned here before;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the onion into the eye, and draw it downwards, and lance with the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not cover up at all the superfluity which is beyond the natural term;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cover it up more, it will spread to the voice and the tongue;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear about cutting, then you should use artifice in the cauterization of the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And the patient should put their head in your hand and then press the tongue onto the instrument that we have said about in the chapter of cautery, and clean with sharp waters, if it is not too thick nor too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and put the handle of this instrument, whose shape is this:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And have the head take on a hair or else put the medicine in it, like the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument all over the medicine onto the eye;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should be seated on his side so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth with the medicine inside, so it does not descend to the throat and the wound.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then take your hand to all the medicine and press it on the eye, for the quantity of half an hour, until you see it become blackened and the irritations from the medicine are calmed.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see [it], take cotton and envelop it on any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument all through the cotton into the eyelid, until the cotton dries on the eye.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and bleed afterwards after four days or five.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	and if you need to start the medicine cautery again, then restart it, and after the cautery apply a poultice around the eye of cotton smeared with butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let them rise from cold water, and be treated with gargling until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, nor than the cautery.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is treated with fumigation in this way, take calaminth and yarrow and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and gather all or some of them together in a pot, and I put ashes in it, and make it boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot be well glazed with hard earth, and inside the pot have a hair-like instrument in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	and it be of silver or lead, and one of the ends be put in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye by means of a cord, until the eyelid is numbified.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after the [vapor] rises again often, until the eyelid dries, and be sure that you do not do this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things happen.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make any cuts where there is an incision of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a cord and put a quill made of egg inside the head, so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the egg quill does not let the foul vapour trouble the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Often it has been used on the throat for a bone or fish spine, or any thing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so then you must try everything that you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see signs of the thing.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what does not appear to you and is returned in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	Perhaps if something becomes loose through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cloth, or a radish root, or a fragment of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie with string to the sponge and then swallow it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes up, if it becomes hardened, and then pull it out;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out as we have said, take the instrument of pincers in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that they can more lightly enter into the throat, and have the head raised high;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all go wrong, nor push the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and make sure that the patient puts in the instrument, so that it is moved with the thing that was swallowed;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If the bowstring is let loose, or if it is pulled further with all the instruments evenly, until it is further.
de la sansue de la gorge	Il semble que nous ayons terminé l'extrait. Voici une traduction plus complète et claire du texte :
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Blood is sometimes medicated in the wound, as I said in the division, by the treatment of remedies;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient in the sunlight, and then press the tongue with the instrument which I told you to.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the pus, then strip it away with each small scabbard, or fine pincers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, then take a horsehair cord and insert it into the patient's throat, then insert the end of the hair cord into hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if it festers the patient with water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full view of cold water and work the mouth, and spit out in her sense not to swallow, and move it to her hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and as soon as the blood feels the water, it will spew.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if she does not spit as we have said, then suffume the patient with assafetida at the instrument which I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will come out without a scar.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a vessel in which there are glowing coals, and it should be covered with a cloth pierced in many places, and within those openings should be the key of the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then you throw your fumigation and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not come out but comes just up to the nose.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and now the sweat will come out and if it does not come out then you start again with the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient suffers from thirst and bitter-sweet things and the like, and he should not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it is necessary for it to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	The form of the instrument with which one treats the swelling is such that, when it can be seen, it resembles bent tweezers for entering the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	And it has the shape of a bee's mouth, and there is a roughness of lime on it, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go.
et vez ci la forme:	and behold this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters about abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Much of the likeness of an abscess is, according to what is remembered hereafter from one and the other in this book, and they are divided into perforation and incision.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two manners of which one is its own likeness, and because of what holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those places where they are within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and the abscesses of the fat part are different from those which come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if an abscess should not be pierced, until the bow is dead according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and there are such as it is necessary to pierce when they are hardened and do not die according to their completion, such as an abscess that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints and are left until they become green around them, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, which is a cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	When the abscess is near the principal member, and you delay the piercing so long that it becomes dead, then harm will come to the principal member.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or if it is near the foundation, if one pierces it while it is still dead;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not necessary for you to pierce an abscess that has become crusty and the digestion is complete, lest the one near the foundation bursts inward and becomes deep-set and a fistula forms;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And you should know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is dead according to accomplishment, and it is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of fever, and the diminishment of pain and redness, and of movement and of becoming smooth of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary for you to set the perforation or more dependent location of the abscess in its place; and where it opens outwards.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the perforation should be long in the body; and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or joints and necks and arteries, or in all places where there is no poultice.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these places, depending on the other member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the fatty part of the body, it is advisable that you leave the puncture open until it has been completely digested, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you make the incision ahead of it, you will loosen the body from the venom in it, and it will be filled with much moisture.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perchance harden the lips and the bottom of it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that needs to be punctured according to the size of the body part, according to what the member in question requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you must bring forth small abscesses, small ulcers.
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large ulcers, and many cracks according to the likeness of the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses which it is necessary to cut out the core and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When he is jaundiced and has become as yellow as a drape, and is wasted, then it is necessary to do just as one does for babies:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if he has such ones that are split into three corners, and those of such kind where one cuts just like the reed of myrtle, as angers' abscesses;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if he has such ones where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who do not have a head, like soft superficial abscesses, you must thoroughly pierce them;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has formed a great swelling, and you pierce it, do not draw out the whole swelling in that hour, but draw out part of it;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess just until the next day, then draw out anything that rises therefrom;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Make this often by degrees, so long as the bowels issue altogether.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	especially if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman bearing, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus is shaken out at times with the issue of the flesh, so that by chance the patient dies, and you do not notice.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Then avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound bursts, and see if the wound of the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a simple incision, then try to close with a linen or old cloth bandage.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is great abscesses, and there are many pustules, then you must put in each one a plug so that they come together against one another.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a piece of raw skin and you have wrapped it around, then you must fill it with old cotton or with some dry rag of linen without moisture, and bind it tight just until the third day.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the bone, and treat with ointment until they are healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is a bleeding in your work, then moisten with cold water and vinegar easily, and soak the cloth in it, and place it on the place bleeding many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the bleeding persists, send for governance and care, and the powders that I have said to be made in a clean place in this book, and if it is the time of summer, and the place or abscess is very nervous, then you should put on tents and wet drapery with wine and hot oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in winter, and the place is fleshy, then you should put on wet drapery with water and oil, or with wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then open up the abscess and bleed it out and treat it, if it is needed, until they are healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this must be understood universally in the treatments of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	I have told you how to proceed with the treatments of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of wounds
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come under the head, and they are of the kind that are like nets, just as the wool of a goat is, and there are many similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are fatty ones and such as also have moisture like boils;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if it has such that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the knife makes an opposite [movement];
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is that you try out every instrument which is called "entromissoire", from which its shape comes after, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then make a cut on top of the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is evacuated, scrape without leaving any of the peel that contains that moisture, for it returns again if you leave anything;
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then plunge cotton in Egyptian balm, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, in water and oil, and apply the dressing to the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and those will cure those who remain overnight.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then reapply the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it will not remain overnight;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound with ointment as is suitable until it is sound.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds its shape well and tightly, cut it off according to this form, a long distance.
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and take out the splinters, and scrape off the scab from all sides, and apply your treatment of drawing forth pus to the breast where it resides.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the vein gives you trouble, do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do likewise with the abscess if it is filled with stone, and from cutting and curing as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cut above the stony abscess and the moist one, if it is lighter, because they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if among these abscesses or on the head of some old woman there is not much moisture, and among those abscesses which I described as being on the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess also like a rough, sharp and white stone that could not be broken.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had struck it with iron, they would have made just as much of a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming from or under the head, such as those that come to the head of children and to the roots of the ears, if the opening is always kept at its most dependent place, so that the fluid can flow out;
et les cure si com il covient.	and they are treated in the manner befits them.
des scrophules	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and inside the groin, and sometimes they come in other parts of the body, and are swollen, and are joined together one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly inside its collarbone, such as the swelling and abscess under the head, just as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and similar forms of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are tumours that contain moisture, and some that are malignant which do not wish to obey good health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one which you see with good disposition at the touch and is similar in colour to the body, and is quiet from every side and is not irate towards the sinews of the neck or the artery or the duct, and is not deep.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	it is necessary that you scrape it off from above, and scrape all around it, and apply the two lips of the cure to the incisions, if you need them, just as we have said in abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and you must take care and little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and it should not be the flesh or cutting, that the hands escape, and do not look too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and that does not let you continue, so put in the wound vinegar to stop bleeding, or some powders that staunch blood, and hold the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it so long as the abscess is calmed down, and the wound becomes softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is staunched, then return to your work, so long as you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then wait until your indicator shows if there are any small scrofulous spots remaining, and cut them out and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if the abscess has a large head in its root, it is not necessary for you to cut into the abscess at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread and let it hang down without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then apply the wound with old cotton steeped in Egyptian oil, then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the whole abscess, it is necessary that you close the two lips of the wound and sew them up now, since there will be no remaining excess because of the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	You must understand to cover the root of it, and to draw out pus, and then close it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those abscesses that contain a suppurative matter, pierce them where they most bleed.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce them in the same way as that previously said, below, then apply linens with oil and similar things, so that they corrupt what remains of the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleansed, then dress it with ointment containing flesh fat until it is healed.
de squinance	of a rupture
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke about the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land do it, and it is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	Those who have swallowed, it is necessary that the cut of the throat which is called "epiglotte" be cleared.
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and so we do not help those who have swallowed it, because all the veins and the body's pores of the patient are hot from the abscess in the mouth or in the throat or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the pulse, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or in four small incisions across, between the two circles or by the size of the incision of a lancet, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and these are advisable for the cutting of the epiglottis that there is no flesh and the vessels are long in depth.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is timid, it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat to its utmost extent, then cut the leather as far as it reaches to the chin.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid letting blood flow if you see anything, then chop off the scab, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the cutting of the vein of the neck which bursts forth through the place that is broken, and by the failure of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and let the wound remain open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed when one doubts strangulation, gather together the two lips of the wound of the jaw, and sew it whole up to the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that make pus form until they are clean.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Alas! I said that we should not do this until the throat is completely closed and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the lack of pulse has been observed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut off the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and therefore the ancients commanded to let the wound remain open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four; and then they commanded that the wound be sewn up and treated, so long as it was cured.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady took a dagger and stabbed it into her throat and cut off part of the channels of the womb.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and I found her in that way as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was issuing from it, and I knew well that it had not been cut too deep nor led very far down to the throat, and the vein was severed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried there, and sewed the wound, and healed her so that she was sound again.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and nothing befell the young lady except that she turned red in the voice, and returned to her normal condition after that.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that there should be no fear in cutting into the epiglotte.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called an "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess of a jasper colour, and it occurs very often in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	and it is according to two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	Innate conditions, and accidents;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or innate has no remedy.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accident is in two manners, one of which resembles an abscess to us, and the other manner is resembling a swelling that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it does not seem wise to work on fire with a fever that is small, and prove and search the entire member;
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it just like a dead abscess, and is not capable of flowing in any way, then drain it, as one drains the head, and treat it to its full depth, if there is no pus.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well through it all, and cure it as befits, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of the fatty tumors
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many kinds of wounds, of which I will say all the likenesses;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now it is necessary for me to say all the distinction which is between cause and effect.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that effect is heat and fever holding on, until the ebullition has passed, and the corruption is accomplished.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the cause there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and the pustule keeps itself, which is its own pouch, and it follows the colour of the body, and also begins like a blister, and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two appearances, either dry or moist, and with much colour as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is fitting, when you come to the treatment of a fatty tumor, that you first inspect and examine it thoroughly with all the instruments which are called "interstitial", according to whether its shape will be circular or oval, which comes afterwards.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses of the neck is that you take or the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your thumbs pincer and pincer, as long as you know that the instruments have pierced the core, then proceed according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the entromissoire, and take care lest it leaps over.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If a moist core runs across the cut, whatever colour it may have, make it like the others that I've said about abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the entromissoire there comes no moisture, know that it is fatty, so make a cross in it, and take hold of the pincers, and scrape it lightly from each part and carry the flax to where it is lodged that you may draw it out sound with the new [thread].
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out sound, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the abscess will return many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little remains and the blood troubles you, fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, hold the wound tight, and put on soothing things warm abscesses, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if it is large, so cut off the two lips of the wound, and cure those which inflame.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein beats against you or is otherwise in opposition, hasten and apply the place of vinegar plaster, and let it be two or three days until the wound purifies, and calm the ebullition of the blood.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cover those which are left from the night.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Behold here the forms of instruments introductive, and they are in three manners:
grans et moien et petit;	great and middle and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and of these there are three square ones which are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and of these there are three manners:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	great, middle, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles for sewing sorcery, and they are of citrine brass or iron or silver, and those that are yellow are more proven to blacken a spot for surrounding the edges of fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	great, medium, and small, according to the size of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of lancets are of many likenesses, just as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	great, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and there are lancets with two edges of three kinds also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and there are lancets with three edges, and they are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and there are lancets with two edges, and single-edged lancets, and they are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these wounds is sharp, and there are some that do not cut very far in one place, from which we peel the nerves, so that we cannot cut the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these instruments are the linen strips repelled by fingers, so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	and they are in three ways:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and middle-sized, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and we do not use any of them farther than is customary in places such as legs and arms and shoulders and hips, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes we make another small instrument resembling peeled reeds, according to this shape, by which we staunch blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is put into the place where there is danger of cutting the veins and arteries, and sometimes they are made in this large shape.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Some men's breasts swell up when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem to be women's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must do so according to this shape from line b to line g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then skin the fat, and fill the wound with medicinal ointment containing charcoal, then sew together the two lips of the wound at the costure, and let it heal until it is sound.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast hangs down and is swollen like women's breasts, make it in two compartments above by two similar incisions.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	in which one is joined to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the longer line contains the shorter according to this shape from line b until line g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about suturing and powders, and everything necessary for the treatment, until they are healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if they are not healed, or the incision is not fully made because the patient will not rest, or due to bleeding, it is necessary that you fill the wound with moistened cotton in corrosive oil;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it so until the remaining flesh and fat rot, then treat it until they are healed.
des apostemes des asselles	the cysts of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These cysts that come under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofulas or nodules, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture need to be cupped according to this form, from the line 2.b. to the line 3.g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.
