puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the doctor treats other wounds until they are healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, then extract with fine pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no distinction between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is in the neck, and there is no other cause except to leave it alone, and not put any restraining thing on it, because it hurts the nerves and makes them retreat;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuance is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but if the medicine is strong, as does chalz boiled in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber also boiled in sweet water, and other stones of myrrh according to this manner, and oily unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and tie it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and the flesh is bare and full of pus, then pierce or cut lower.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is severed and bleeding comes from it, then tie off, apply a compress, and cauterize as necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the throat is severed or the windpipe, and the conduit is kept, by which the flesh goes, then cut the windpipe on the dog's neck, and do not touch the throat but place it according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it properly, and leave it for some days, then heal with ointments from decaying so long as they are healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then scrape it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, then remove all that you can, and leave what you cannot get out, so that the wound becomes foul, and is opened and cleaned up the opening.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on top of it the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has formed an abscess, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a blow from a lance or a sword, and the wound is deep, see if there are gas bubbles rising from the wound as the patient swells.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it at the first hour nor bind it for the blood which will not stay inside and return to the heart and kill the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I put attractive ointment on it, and bind it two times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep over the wound three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	If there will come no spasm, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor straining of the muscles.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure him with bindings and other treatments, until he be healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal or function, then know that there is an abscess.
si la cure si com on doit.	if the treatment is done as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is a cut from a sword or knife and it is superficial, or worse on the back or rear, then treat the one that is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, stitch it.
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, with powder; and if it has been pressed into the bone, and there are splintered pieces, then clean the wound, and remove the foreign bodies if they are detached.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not severed, then let the wound rot, and it will facilitate extraction;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other members, it is a judgment such as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of intestinal rupture.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great and middle-sized and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from a great wound sometimes the intestines or the membranes of the intestines protrude, by which their introduction occurs.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes it turns out worse than a small wound compared to a great one, therefore one sets the intestines in with pins if one does not set them in warm together.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, they set in better with pins, and because of this it is more advantageous to sew the middle wound, therefore one sews the intestine back into place before the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to IV manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common stitches occur in the belly's tear, and the stitch of other wounds of the body and two other proper stitches are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and notwithstanding they are more proper with the belly's stitch, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestines comes out, and what needs to be done is easy, it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are inflamed from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	soak a sponge or a moist cloth in tepid water only, or boil it in hot water with cypress and spikenard, and warm the intestine until the swelling is removed.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and at any time done this wine restraining, and is made that he has sole for to unswell.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling departing, so moisten the intestines with hot water or ale and badly cooked vegetables, for by them is closed up the entrance to the place of things.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, so make a pit in the wound with the instrument with which we scrape off ulcers.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is made that one cut, which no one should cut unless there is great necessity that it be done;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so cut inside in the curve and not outward, and behold the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have burst forth, then restore them to their natural form in their proper place, if you are able, for this is worth striving.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the belly, it behooves you to make the patient lie on his back, and set his legs higher than his head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part below the belly, so set the head and pelvis higher than the parts below, and also the curvature of the belly will be in one of the two parts so that the injured part will be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to remember what I say about great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds place the dressing that is attached to you, then take between your hands the minister's patty which covers the entire curvature at his hand, and put together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common manner of stitching, and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound a double thickness, and stick in a needle where there is good thread strong;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two keys of the skin with the two keys of the leather, which is beneath the skin inside, as far as you make it pierce from that part, and put together the two heads of the leather the four parts;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then tie with a doubled thread around the needle of two parts, then join together the two bones of the wound properly, and then let them be for two days' space, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then tie the thread double as you have done for the first needle, and cease not to do this with the needles, so long as all of the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be of medium size between fine and thick, for the fine needles pierce all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot well enter;
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be medium-sized;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it does not seem good to thrust the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and open up the wound in front of the suturing;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then remove the points of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and put tents or a cloth over the points of the needles to keep them steady, and let them be until the wound is sutured;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this manner of stitching with needles is more advisable for small wounds, because it suffices with one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common, and it consists of assembling the two pieces of leather and the two pieces of skin together with one needle where there is a strong thread in the middle.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced these pieces together, then draw out the needle at the part where you began, in the manner that one sews cloth.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a thread of the thickness of a small thimble between each stitch.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	this stitch is known to men, and I sewed a wound that a man had on his belly, which was hurt by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm in width, and the intestines were well exposed two palms in width, and the wound was within the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back his intestines after he had been without them for 24 hours and the wound was sown up just to 15 days, and he cured it, and was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physician had judged that he was going to die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not cure him with ointment, for I was in such a place where one could not find any, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and placed some old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed him with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and push it through from the outer part just to the inner part;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced through right to right, then bring the end of the thread or cord that you have passed the needle through, and make it pierce from the inner part just to the outer part;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this stitching is that you stitch in such a way as clothiers make felt, and that you leave one end of the thread once, and take it up again on the other side, until the stitching is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of sewing, which the Greeks call properly, is so that some do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the silk to the other end.
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	stitch a needle or end of the thread nearby, and make a small hole in that place alone, and leave the two ends of the silk;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle, and make a hole through from the outside part just up to the inside part, with the two ends of the silk.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make a hole in one and the other from the outside part just up to the inside part, through two other eyes of the thread that are on the opposite side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the mother manner of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	The Greeks say this phrase, and some bear witness to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, or have thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	One must stick one needle here, and the other there, in the manner of those who sew corsets.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and you should know that when a rupture is inside the belly, the suturing is more grievous than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, just as if fire had changed it, then set the intestines and the gut in place again.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put powder on the charred part, and if fire has changed it, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and sew the thread, and close the stitches of the gash, and the tear.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound just like the others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	If you don't have medicine, put on it cotton cloth as soon as the boil starts to burst; and rub it with it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For in many simple wounds you don't need any other medicine besides this.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound may bring on community among the principal members, then it is necessary for you to soak linen cloth in warm temperate oil or in rose oil and put it around the groin and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if he feels pain or putridness in the bowels and it often happens, then cleanse him with a suppository of old vinegar wine, and similarly if the putridness comes as far as the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and puncture it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is more easily to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are injured, and it is because of the fragility of their veins that are within them, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the approach of its nature to those places.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine falls out of the wound, then put it back as well as the intestine does itself while still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has become green or black, then you must tie the place that is black so that bleeding does not occur there, for there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut out what is between the bandage, and let the two ends hang down from beneath the wound to its edge in order to lighten the extraction when the intestine falls, and the wound swells.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, one can restore it in some people, for I have seen a man wounded by a spear in his belly.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right of the stomach and became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and from it there came purging and vomiting.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied a treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease subtlety until they were healed, and the joints tightened.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it tighten, I doubted that the patient would be ill in his belly.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was not a thing wrong with him, but he remained in better disposition, and eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experienced people said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take lint or flax from great thorns, then bind the lips of the wound together, and when the lint has opened its mouth, put it on top of the two lips, so that it tightens its mouth over.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then the physician binds the head, and it stays like that so it cannot be undone, and then puts another piece of flax after in this manner as before, until the wound is completely closed.
et cout la plaie.	And apply a poultice to the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the head of a [?] ( likely an arrow or other sharp object) is stuck in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and it can be bound with a thread from the gut of an animal that has been sewn up in the same way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this thread from intestine that is completely unthreaded, and then tie to the head of this thread a fine linen thread twisted into a cord, then insert the thread in the needle and sew up the intestine, and tighten the thread in the running stitch;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of sewing with thread is not different from the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the outer intestines, and there is no remedy or healing, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is called "fistula" universally; and just as much so when it breaks out and runs with pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to its hard and white nodule formation absent pain, and it is also hairy like the plumage of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in clear bowel, and other times thickened;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and other times rather large;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed and there is no flesh, it is due to one of the nine causes;
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the thinness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its foulness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because it has hard flesh inside and above the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much pus;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the wound is foul and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	the medicine is not good in treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or on account of the property in that region is slow the digestion and delays health and flees by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes and signs and remedies of medicines in the section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And now it is fitting that I make you aware of the treatment of fistula which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	know that fistula occurs in every member of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come to the large veins and arteries and nerves or to the uterus or to the intestines or to the bladder or to some of the ribs or to the spine of the back or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and so too that comes to the property of the principal member and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas of this type are grievous to heal, and there is no other treatment but purging, and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the exact place I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you recognize it, then take a tent of tin or iron, if the fistula is straight, then scrape.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is twisted, then search for a thin tent of lead, because the lead bends more easily around the twisting.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it by tents, then cleanse it through one of the openings, because the moisture runs from one opening to another, and purify.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then scrape the fistula to your ability, and know if there are bones or nerves, and go deep enough, and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where it is.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or a vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then treat it according to what I have said, and remove the abscess and the corrupted flesh that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep in a straight place, then you should fill it deeply, as long as you can, then put wet compresses on medicinal dough, and plug them up right to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the remaining superfluity that is at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put unguents in fresh healthy flesh, as long as it remains healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if they are not healed by those things, then cauterize them as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then fill it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If you wish to open or cut the vein, or principal limbs, as we have said.
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then remove it as long as the corruption is entirely removed, then treat with remedies that cause fresh flesh until they are healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if they are not healed and return to their former state, know that you have not gone all the way to the source.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it is uncovered and you search until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then put back in its place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if they are thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to let it go as it will by nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupted bone and you can draw it out with forceps, then pull it out to the suitable instrument for that; and if there are many bones, then pull them all out, do not leave any one.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture causes contractions, and there is no error or fear, then cut and scrape and remove the flesh.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put on the wound something causing a stench to purify it, and let it stay until the place around the bones is purified, and then the bones will be easier.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, then clean only the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is great part of the corrupt matter and comes just to the surface of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then you must scrape and cut all up to the corruption, and then heal it until it is sewn together.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of an ulcer that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came inside the body, so much so that materials came to the leg and he was swelling with a large abscess, and he did not have any reason outside for it to be opened.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the surgeon, due to their foolishness, operated so much on top that the abscess was opened, and a lot of materials flowed out, and it became a fistula, and there came out many perforations from which all manner of bad odor and moisture were coming from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many surgeons put cure around two years, and there was no wise person in the art of healing, until I was called to it, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what flowed from the perforations into the body.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the boy's body became red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and I found that one was facing the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I quickly ran then and scraped in one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and I found it to be corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came right up to the inside of the bone.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I scraped away what appeared from the corrupted bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption, except for the one I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and then I began to restore the wound with medicinal salves over a long time, and it would not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I started again, and scraped away the bone as before, and I found the continued corruption in the bone, and I scraped it and then removed it, and I decided to heal the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I was unable until I scraped around one palm's width of the bone, and treated it all the way to its center, then restored it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and he was healed and sewn up quickly, and it did not need to be done again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For it was that often the bleeding led to evacuation of blood, but he became entirely cured, and in place of the bone there grew a hard flesh, and it turned out to be of good disposition and caused no harm nor any adverse effect at all, neither when he came nor went.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it should be sewn up in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take a lien, and hold it at the head of the bone that is open, and instruct someone to stretch it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another lien of thicker linen than the first lien, and tie it above the flesh that is over the bone, and stretch the head, so that you pull out the corrupted flesh below, and uncover the flesh on the place where you see to sew, that the sewing does not harm the flesh;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a hot iron or a wooden tablet under the bone in order to melt and cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to clean as much as can be seen and felt the corruption, and clean again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupt, and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover the flesh entirely.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place a brander below it, and then clean the corruption from one part to another; and make the cleaning go as deep as the depth of the corruption can reach, if possible, just as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupt joint and clean the bone on the other side where it contains.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the connection of the two joints, then there's no other remedy but to cut them.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the joint of the hand or in the joint of the foot, it's very strong that thing, but still you must inquire about that ulceration how it opens up.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way you can, but do not let the vein or nerve be against you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incisors and hair-like threads for covering bones are numerous, according to the seat of the bone and its appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare the instrument suitable for each appearance of work;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument needed, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if thou thinkest of the instrument needed according to what is necessary.
dou feu	from fire (i.e. a hot iron or ember)
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The joints may become dislocated either due to an internal cause or a external one;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you will have medicated that corruption with the cure of medicines, and it does not help, then it is necessary to cover that member up to its place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient may escape from death or from the greater evil, the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the members become black, so that it seems they are burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corrosive of the member to the member spreads, and takes throughout the body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if you hasten to cover it, and if it is due to the bite of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, if the corrosion is on the head of the vein, if you cut it, and do not give it space to come until the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, then cut it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, then cut it in the armpit;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the armpit, it is death, and there is no remedy except by the quantity of its venom.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do the same for all joints if there comes a gangrene of the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes on the foot, then cut all of the foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up to the thigh, then cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy except letting the patient die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the manner of cutting or sawing the member is that you bind it up and down, and extend one servant's strap below, and another servant's strap above, and you cut away the flesh which is between the two straps, as wide as a broad spatula, so that the bone be uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or saw it, and put a linen cloth on each side, so that the saw may not touch the healthy place, and another lesion and abscess will come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	If hemorrhaging comes from the cut while you work, then quickly cauterize the place or put on some restraining powders;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened at my house in Saumur:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	a blackness appeared that seemed like burning fire, and this corruption came first to his right heel, until it consumed the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he quickly had the foot cauterized and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long afterwards the corruption came back to his right hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things that were counter-acting after the cleansing of the body, but the corrosion could not be ceased;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, that I had hope of recovering the substance.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the strength of the man was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he entirely despaired and returned to his land and had himself cut off his hand and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not made this up other than for the things that one does to another person when necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess forms in fatty flesh and stays so long that it makes a large gathering of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they rot and burst, and the pus leaps out, and the place remains empty, just like a wineskin.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin above is just as delicate as a loose, fine cloth, and they do not run all the way to the bone or to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain", and it is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it reaches just to the bone deep inside, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure is that you bind him all around with that skin, and in the same way as you would with a bandage.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it is not done for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have a suspicion that the skin is corrupted, and the corruption is not deep inside, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it with a poultice.
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	examine if the breast is large and the nipple that comes out of it has a foul smell, then treat it with Egyptian medicine which is made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take assafetida, oil, and lye, in equal amounts, and put the mixture to cook in one vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and also becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take as much as you need from them, and make it in water and honey, and make a suppository for the breast, and hold the fistula;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay inside for 2 hours, then squeeze it out;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is cleaned and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and at any time make a suppository of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and take ash from grapevine wood, pour water on top, then let it settle, and use it as a suppository, until you know that the breast is well cleaned;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then make a suppository with water and honey or put a little bit of litharge in it;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	You mix a poultice of honey and wine sweetened; that the honey has the property to cleanse and purify, and the wine makes the blood warm.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this and are sure that the wound is well cleansed, make a poultice with what brings pus to rise in it; and take diaphinite plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	you mix a poultice of certain medicines and ointments, whose properties I have said to treat with ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the sore of the breast is small and the poultice cane cannot enter, then enlarge it with a little iron piece and put on a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too wide, then shape it and leave just so that the poultice cane can enter; and if the pit that spills pus is above, then cut or lower it to where it should be.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowstring is quite loose, do not let hair grow;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cover the breast from below as you see, prepare it in such a manner that the bowstring runs to its lowest point; for when the bowstring is quite loose, do not let hair grow and if you cannot cover the breast from below as you see, prepare it in this manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the bowstring runs lightly downward, and leave nothing hanging from the bowstring;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to place on the shoulder, and lay them on a linen cloth that covers all the shoulder;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cover the strongest part of the breast where the hole of the shoulder is, making it larger than the first, then apply soft ointment on the other cloth according to the size of the hole, and put it on the hole of the shoulder to loosen the bowstring, and do not remove the large cloth outside which once a day for many days;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and the one who is on the pertuss of the breast, often removes it to remove the bow; and know what has come out of the bow; if it's venom or pus or plenty or digestible or indigestible.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not; and when your medicine has spread in such a manner that you see what kind of nature comes up on the breast's pustule, then know that the breast has been hurt already, and approach the physician.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then dress it in the morning or on the third day; and when you remove the dressing from the wound, if there is another cloth covering, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast spatters indigestible pus after many days, know that the breast has not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons stay behind after a long time, do not despair of health, for the healthy approach.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men whose wounds become inflamed with pus in them, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if his undigested bile comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast has not been hurt.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the wound is slow to heal and suppurating, then add medicinal ointments that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diachite ointment, for it has a great part of vitriol, and this is the final remedy.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diachite ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and equal parts of old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then cook it and apply it.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and this same thing makes better cooked and thickened honey, when diachite ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and frankincense, and grind them, and powder over the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then bind it in a linen cloth, and stretch it over the wound, and sometimes administer an Aristolochia longa, and roots of the heavenly lily, which is also like flour of vitriols and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and with simple or compound ointments:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them and make a powder and put on the honey that I said to use.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the wound is long and not healed by this treatment, then know that the corruption is deep within and has pressed into the bone, or hardened the members, or formed a lump.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the ulceration of the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil on the arm (ungle).
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Pain or boil is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or foot, or perhaps in other places.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is neglected and becomes old, then the abscess breaks out and bursts forth, and pours out pus as far as it can reach the root of the nail, and perhaps all the way through.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes a corrosion just up to the bone, so that it causes stinking pain, and the eye of the tooth is wide open, and the color is foul.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit at all, then you must cut out from it entirely the surplus matter that is left of the boil, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterizations are very great help if the bone is sound, and the nail is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail pierces the flesh, and starts to point it, and lacerates it, then you should put a hot instrument under the nail that pierces the flesh, and push it upwards, and gently scrape away that flesh with scorching and corrosive medicines in order to remove all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then scrape it away and follow up with a treatment, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the tooth corrupting, then scrape out the marrow just as has been said before, and treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is abscessed, and pus-filled, and he feels great pain, then you should drain it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the angle of the splint at an angle across it; and make sure that the cut does not come all the way to the flesh which is below the joint, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if there is [a problem], then put something on top which calms it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of deafness in the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The nails which grow on the hands of some men by chance are entirely fleshy, and sometimes there is a toe in place of one, and occasionally an awn, and once in a while the birth is in the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of the nails.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born in any part of the shoulder or upper arm do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the shoulder, by chance they do move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut of that which is fleshy is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at the root with a wide splint.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those who are born in the root of the joint are heavy to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	if it holds onto you to cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In that which is born or stuck in the lower navel, it is necessary that you cut first around the flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable string for this, then heal him until he is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come to the bones in the joints occur by birth, or from a wound, or from being burned with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut the suture, so that it can be repaired according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then put between two tents or damp cloths soaked in rose oil, so they will not stick together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of cloth, until the place is closed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a wound comes to any of his knees with the palm, then bind that wound in the same way.
des vils	the ulcers
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Fevers are swollen and covered with superfluities of melancholy humours that come on in many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to them an occasional purging with vinegar, and then salve with the oil of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The cure by iron is according to two manners:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that you cauterize them and draw out the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you let the vein bleed completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cut is according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	wash the leg first with hot water very strongly, until the thick blood is thinned, then hold the patient's leg steady from above the knee as far as the part below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in I place, or in II, or in III, with a large knife, then raise and pull out the black blood to your hand, from one end just to the other, as much blood as the patient's virtue can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it, and instruct him to eat meat that is being dripping with cold black bile;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and resume the evacuation and the cleansing when the veins are empty, and it brings harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The remedies of the eyes according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair on it, then put it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water as long as it becomes red, and swell the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut in that place where the vein is long at the top of the kneecap, or in the part under the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then cure the skin with vinegar, and scrape the vein from all sides, until it appears when one feels it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and we see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks just like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then insert the needle underneath, until it is raised above the skin, and then dip it in vinegar lightly, then bind it back in its other place on three threads;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it up to the needle, just as you did, and dip it in another vinegar, just as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then bind another cloth, or more if you need it, then lift it and bind to the foot, then pull and lift just to the second cloth;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull it from cloth to cloth, until it comes out all clear, then bind it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot pull it out and lift it, then place a sharp needle on the very strong doubled thread, tie it and pull, and place it under the thread, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and take care that it does not snag, for if it snags, then one cannot pull it out or lift it, and harm will come to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have pulled it all out, place moistened wool on the wound site in wine and rose oil.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and care for him until he is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it obliquely, but do not cut into it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and pull it out just as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one pokes the vein is curved, and does not cut, so that it may poke the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of thick curvature, for if it were thin, it would poke the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of civil veins
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in hot places where herbs and trees do not grow, and on earth where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it may be found in other places than the legs, and this occurs because of the putridity that comes from under the skin, just as snakes and worms are embedded between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this swelling are such that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then the place changes, and the swelling begins to come out, just like a root from a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the joint opens, you must wrap it around a piece of linen cloth that is one and a half ells in length up to two ells, and the noue, and leave the linen cloth hanging down from the leg, and every time it gets loose, you must rewrap it around the linen cloth, and the noue.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut a part of it off, and wrap the remaining part around it, and do not cut it in its root, until it comes out entirely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, then it will penetrate into the flesh, and cause an abscess and putrefaction at the place, and a bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	on account of which thing it is necessary to treat it little by little just up to the head, and let nothing remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and this vein is sometimes so when it is treated to the length of two palms or ten, and a man came to me whose came out to ten palms long, and when you cut it, it bursts through a hole or pustule, and pierces just up to its bottom, so that everything comes out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and when it is empty the matter which is inside, and apply medicines to the place that prevent putrefaction for any day, then cure it just like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And at this wound there are often many discharges, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or leg, or elsewhere on the body, where there is much pus, and from which there are discharges.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Then cure it as we have said beforehand.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "disease of the ox" because it often occurs with cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes all over the body rising and descending, and causes pain to move from member to member, until it bursts the skin where it goes, and discharges.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is a sign of corruption of some humour, such as comes with worms and serpents and lice and ascarids from the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts its wickedness, because when it goes through the body and rises to the head and comes into the eye, by chance it enters and destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and it occurs often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him cured and healed, one cannot be certain until he walks:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so then you must tie the place above and below with a strong tight band, then sew on top and let it heal, and if the abscess is very deep in the flesh, and you do not find it, then burn it with fire on top until it suppurates;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it blinds the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or approaching the eye close up, then press the eyelid firmly over it and sew on top, and let it heal.
