et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to instruct the patient in cleansing of the body with soluble medicines for bad humors that are born within him, and abstain from strong meats causing corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land; it is a pain that occurs in certain members, and can move from member to member.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to an ailing woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the middle of her upper arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and I saw it spread after that, up to the shoulder, just as quickly as a worm spreads out, or like bright silver when it moves from place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain moved away from that place and settled in the shoulder, and then a little after it ran through the whole body, so that it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	and then she told me that it was twisting again around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in such a way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I had always believed that the pain moved from one place to another well, but I did not believe it so, as I saw in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought it was because of this that the woman had a dry body and the veins were discovered, and because of this there appeared that constrained windiness.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they did not appear in those who are well-nourished, and who have moist bodies and responding veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see curing this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, tie on top and below hastily, and then strike above until the constrained windiness is driven to its proper place.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the spot;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your own eyes, then have the patient cured by those who purge the windiness, such as stinking pills, and dragon's breath pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Splinters are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversities of them are that there are those with great points, small ones, hairy ones, and blunt ones;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those with two angles, and of those with wings, and of those with pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which slips into any member so it slips in two manners:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or into the principal member that drops, such as brain, heart, liver, womb, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it slips then in any place of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you afterwards becomes apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for many die afterwards in various conditions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces it and perforates the bone, and shoots out the splinter which is above the brain, is when there is scotoma and swoon and vomiting and vertigo in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of gall.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perchance it will burst from the nostrils, or the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps speech and voice are lost.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there is an effusion of white moist discharge from the wound, resembling pus, and also it jumps like a boil on flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if you notice these signs, then hold back from the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the arrowhead when it penetrates into the heart are that it is close to the left breastbone, and feels as though it was stuck in a hard, not empty thing.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrowhead becomes putrid like pus, and there is black bloody discharge, and comes forth cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	therefore know without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the splinter when it lodges in the liver is that bloody foam bursts out from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the sick person changes color, and gasps for breath and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrowhead falls into the covering of the liver, it is near to the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	And throws a great anguish and great pain and sighs;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and moves all the limbs of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the splinter lodges in the stomach, perhaps something that is undigested meat comes out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the splinter lodges in the belly and comes out through the intestine without any signs of digestion, then there is no hope for a cure or for extracting the splinter.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if an arrowhead pierces the bladder and the urine bursts out and comes forth, and the patient feels strong pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and forearms and calves and legs and similar parts, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the splinter is in a nerve or artery and it is venomous, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man whose arrow pierced the tear in the root of the eye:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I attempted it and I pushed it out on the other side through the fatty part of the ear, and he was healed without a scar.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I drew out an arrow that had pierced the fatty part of the eye under the eyebrow and the arrowhead was repelled, and I could only reach as far as the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large enough for a Turkish bow, completely iron, without ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The game was made whole, and no evil accident came to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And draw out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was the Arab arrow at the ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I softened the points, and sharpened them until I drew it out, and the Christian was made whole.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I drew an arrow from the man, who had been pierced in the belly, and thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then that it had passed thirty days, his condition did not change.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow and cauterized it, and drew it out, and there was no evil accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see the man to whom an arrow had fallen on the back, and the wound was sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural conditions, nor found any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And he saw another man to whom an arrow was shot in his face, and the wound was sewn up.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and it remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And he shot an arrow into the king of the princes, who was standing in his neck, and it was somewhat leaning to the right side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was entirely removed.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat him after it had been lodged for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched the whole body with a subtle tent, and did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and hurt below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I put on him a plaster attracting and digesting, so that the place would not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the wound of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the poultice many times, and the wound was resolved again, and so the patient remained for a long time until he felt the arrow inside his body one day.
et il le me dist.	and he told me to it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied on the wound a medicinal juice that corrodes by many times, until it was open, and I probed, and felt the head of the arrow which had grown into place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I pushed into the opening of the wound with that corrosive juice, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and the tip of the arrow broke off well in four months, and then the wound that I had hammered with pincers and twisted on both sides could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Then I did not cease to perfect and devise ways of instruments, until I took it one day with good pincers, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, so that I could extract and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the sages judge that a nasal catheter cannot restore:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you can place your treatment on what I do not say at all, for books cannot take in everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but wise masters gather well on small things, and on what is currently present and lacking, they find new work, and new instrument, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not emerge from limbs where they are stuck unless according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or from their natural place or on the other side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which springs out from its natural place is an arrow entering into fleshy places and springs forth at least once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not spring out now, then leave it so long as the flesh around it is putrid and the opening is closed.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, then leave it so for some days and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it springs out, and if it does not spring out, then pierce around with a very sharp point, so that the place around it is widened, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes just to one of the hollows of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If one does not pull it out, but lets it remain until it is even after some days, because if the arrow comes as far as the skin, it is a death sentence.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone alone and does not go up to the brain, and the patient remains some days without bad accident, then the instrument for drawing it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very deeply inserted and cannot come out further, I administer hot poultices around it, as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the spot until it is sound.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is reset in its place within the body and cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the tent.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, pull it out with any convenient instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no artery or nerve or vein, then file it down until the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears where it holds on, cut away the flesh that is stuck to the two parts as far as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And take care to break the arrow shaft carefully; and draw it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot get it out at once, leave it until the area around the wound is purged, then pull it out, because the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding is contrary, then take care of what we have said in its chapter about the cure.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of the incision near the nerve and vein, and think how you can draw out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and set the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him, for that is the greatest aid it can be; and if you cannot do this, then set him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or if it has pierced anything of him, or the skin is inflamed in place where one can see it or feel it apparently.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	cut then up so that the pincers can take hold, and then pull it out.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If the spring is now swollen.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, so that it goes into the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, let her wait a bit longer and then continue to extract it until it swells again;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow head is in there, push all of the shaft in;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft bends and you wish to administer an ointment, give it the instrument which is curly, so that the point of the arrowhead goes into the curly part of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then push it in and if the arrow is bent, give it the instrument with an entering point, to make the extraction easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you cut out all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as is fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is in the chest or belly or bladder or side and it is close to the surface, and you can cover over it, then cut;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, and then pull it out, and then sew up the wound if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment continues until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers with which one pulls out needles are like the beak of a bird, and see here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many methods:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	great, unusual, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feathers of a bird, to guide towards the tip of the arrow, such as this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of pliers in order to bend and test if this is so:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the strings of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of veins from which one becomes well are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen at the head, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	two vessels that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two visible temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two corners of the two eyes, which are called "aspires".
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the veins that are at the back of the neck.
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two tendons that are in the neck.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the lips of the mouth, and they are called "augeherich".
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins which one commonly drains are like a "V" in each arm.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the median one is called "facia", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and the common people call it "vein of the heart".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic vein is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the elbow, and it is that one which drains, which opens obviously above the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the saphena vein is the vein which is between the ring and middle fingers, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and at the foot are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	One is under the curvature of the pocket of the left side, and the second saphena which is at the ankle of the right side.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that is called "nisse", which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The swellings of the veins that are behind the ears so aid against quinsies in old people and against migraine;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the salve so that I tell you is to raise the head of the patient and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then bind the patient's neck with a screw until the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent places of the head;
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	heat them then to your elbow and where you feel the lump under your elbow, make it sign that it is heated.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet and insert it below the vein up to the bone. Then lift your hand all along the vein upwards and cut through the skin and the vein very well. Then cause blood to issue forth until you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then bind it tightly so that it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incision and cauterizing in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The sinew of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth for the old eye disease and soreness and habitual obtalmia and sharpness at the eyes' corners.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the surgeon if it is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient bind their neck so tightly that both veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse below your throat and then sign for it to stop;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then lift the knife up onto the vein in the upper part of your thumb, and place the lancet below, and lift the vein up, and close it, just as you have done with two other veins, and stop the bleeding as needed.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, and place your thumb over the vein for an hour, then put on a cloth.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then tie it up firmly, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The vein bleeding of the forehead is just as valuable as the phlebotomy of the cerebral vein in ancient diseases of the face, and in migraine, and in jaundice.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patient twists his neck so tight that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "digger", whose shape is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, letting two blood flows come out according to how much you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then untie the patient's collar and tie the vein so that it is stopped bleeding and at no time does a wide flow occur.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it is not necessary for the flows to be too abundant;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and let it bleed across, because the bone is near, and by chance break the flow when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the armpits helps them, and the itch, and the roseola, and the oriental sickness in the eye, and the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient strains his neck by twisting with some thread, just as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then let it bleed, and let the blood flow freely, a little long like a flame, a little wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are fine, by chance they break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then stop the bleeding of the blood, as long as you need to, and then bind it on cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The bleeding of the vein of the neck is worth against a fever, and against severe sweating, and against face diseases, such as headache and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient will tighten their neck, then strain their head to your left hand, and take out the thin flame long, and put it between the lip in the space which is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will start to stop now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too far into depth, and make a careful cut of the blood according to your need, then bind it up for one night, because it is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The juice of the two kinds of ivy helps in the tightening of the spleen, and at the beginning of healing, and for many diseases, and for inflammation, and for corrosion, and for herpes, and boils;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the juice is that the patient stretches his neck under both of them, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on the stool, then bleed the vein from the long one somewhat broadly, then draw out the blood temperately, or as long as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then redo the other part in the other vein, then loosen the ligament, and hold the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let him be until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the washing of books (or possibly "of book remedies")
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins on the upper lips helps to cool the mouth and corrupt the gums, and split the lips, and cause the nose to bleed inward.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of healing is to have the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip and look at the two veins, of which one is on the right side and the other on the left, and know them by this that they are black, and by this that around them are small dark veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then mark one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then mark the largest of each side, and do it with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the washing under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The veinous purgation that is below the tongue helps after the bleeding of the head; and it is to the constriction of the throat, and the diseases of the eye, and the diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the purger are that the patient sees between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts their tongue, and looks down on each side for a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	purge then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the throat from which one purges commonly are purged in two manners:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by pricking with a sharp flame-edged lancet or an olive-like subtle lancet such as those cutting cutters, and it is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are large and subtle according to the largeness and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the lancet is very well known, and it's large as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open veins with thick clear blood visible, and those that contain thick blood and turmoil.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive-shaped flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it's more delicate and pointed, and it's for bleeding the small veins where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with ailments that are under the throat, and at the neck, and at the chest, and at the belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon to make an incision, and to beware of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and bleeding from blood comes, then he must staunch it, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and he should not grasp the flame, but rather cut with a steady hand.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open obviously, then you must extract it and change to another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want to take any blood from it, or draw out the venous blood from the arm.
elle apert manifestement;	it appears visibly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cauterize with a flame in the shape of a silversmith's bellows, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the site of the vein, it is then necessary that you stretch out the arm and touch the place until you feel the hairs.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the site of incision and then bind the arm and cauterize the vein with a flame in the shape of a silversmith's bellows.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the site swollen, for it is the artery:
eschui la donques.	avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it come out in the same way as a child's urine and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and put on your bandage for a long time; then remove it if the blood has stopped.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Secure the arm well, and let it be so, and do not move the patient's limb.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and he should be on his back, and not move until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood is not stopped and he complains, and medical aid is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, because the head of the vein retreats.
et estainche li sans.	and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of birch bark, and split it, and take one half and bind well just up to the other end.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the bleeding has stopped, that is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then apply the powder which stops blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stitches are not at all glued in more positions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the tendon of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein of the neck in middle position so helps that it treats blood from the top of the head and from the trunk below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the vein stripper that he beware of the nerve which is below, and if he pierces too deeply, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the stitches will be glued, and perchance he cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve opens very often, and if it does not open in any man because of its subtlety, then you must loosen the stitches of the instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and release the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The fluid of the head so aids, that it draws blood from the head, and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to cleanse with burning olive oil or burning myrtle, for this is the most safe of all the veins, because there are no nerves nor arteries beneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, it is necessary to seek out the most lightweight location, and harm nothing if one fails the first time, and one recommences;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance the places swell in some men when one fails the first time, but it harms nothing.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing that you must know to clean is that cleansing is not done forcefully except to preserve health, and to prevent illnesses from coming;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the cleansing be done in one of the three veins which are on the neck:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, facial, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should cleanse oneself at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after meals, when the signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should purify oneself on the first day or third, after 2 hours or 3 days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The purification administered to the sick has no fixed hour, but when need arises by day or night, at all hours and in all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not necessary to purify children until the age of XIV, nor a woman bearing fruit that she has conceived for less than 7 months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly be bled who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wants to purify themselves, however it may be, they should first cleanse the intestines with a light suppository, if they have much bad humors retained, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the superfluous things which harm the main members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	One does not become well again who is too full of meat, nor one who is drunk, as long as he remains in that state, nor one who is dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one has been sick with a stomach ailment, and vomiting, and purging of the belly, and multiplying in intercourse with a woman, and labor, wakefulness, and hunger, and all that virtue, or by something of the arm or from the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtilly purge the humors, if the blood is thick, by means of meat and drink and medicine, if you have the power to do so;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter the bath, if no obstacle is in the way, to subtly let out the blood, and heal the vein of the belly around the third part, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself that day from labor, and from pain, and from lust, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be at ease and tranquil; and the bandage should be higher than the one who is being bled, and the cloth wipe the arm two or three times, then draw out the thread slowly above, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot stop the blood.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then wipe the place with hands so that the veins swell and feel it.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then wet the bandage with the flame of a spoonful of old oil, then place the tip of your left hand on the vein below the place where you want to bleed, so that the vein does not flow and break when it is pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flow as strings when bleeding, and those of such a nature that are full of venosity, so that when you put the flame on them, they recoil from the flame and cannot be opened, and thus it is with these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if the vein is opened too much, then the wound is too narrow, so it is necessary that the surgeons be wise in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens at the first time, that's good.
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, it continues again in another place near that spot or on high speed, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the swelling remains and the patient grows anxious, let him leave it alone for one day or two, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps then foul abscesses will come.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter in the bath, and then let him make another incision if he likes.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, cut through it subtly and you doubt that there is not so much blood as you see, then make a straight incision in that same opening itself.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and do the work with a little haste, so that the swelling may remain.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for it often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the joint swollen, do not start to cauterize again, and put on a little bit of linseed oil, for it lightens the body of blood, and is a binder in this swelling of the lymph that oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the linseed oil in each cauterization that you do for the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same thing is done with triacle and poppy, when it is put on the joint.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if you cut off the blood clot and separate it when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a large abscess which often happens, just when the incision of the vein is small or only once cauterized, you hasten and put on the joint a moist sponge in hot water and in silk for a short hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the bleeding of the vein, and if it stays in place for several days with no blackness or greenish color, then it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place on something made of aloes or myrrh, mixed with juice of camphor, onion, or similar thing.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times there occurs an abscess and appearance like the sepsis of the spleen;
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	place then your hand on it, and if you find it soft to the touch of the hand when compressed, that is bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	be careful then that you do not place on anything of what we have said, for it is possible to cut the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but make a dry compress to harden the place, then apply another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each bleeding in proportion to its quantity and virtue, and according to the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	If the blood is black, let it come out until it turns red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see the pus (or discharge) thick, let it come out until it becomes subtlered.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for him who is full (or swollen) and flat, and has need of bloodletting, that a larger wound be made in him, and the flaps (or loose skin) be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and have him heal quickly and often, and one must heal him by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of healing saves from hemorrhaging and tearing of nerves, and is worth more than long or wide healing.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for him whose body fails to heal, it is necessary to give moist bread in juice of unripe pomegranate;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is overheated, have him drink blood 3 times or 4; And if he has a cold complexion, have him drink in front of the surgeon's pan sweetened with honey syrup, or with aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he vomits at the sainie, after the spilling of much blood, it is necessary that he drink a broth of meat and a sweet-smelling syrup and use other things which we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to move his arm and heal another time, so it must be, when it is weakened by great blood loss, that he heals gradually little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to move his arm after the first healing, and he has strong vigor, then it heals within 7 hours after the first healing, or within the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to heal from another side, then he must heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood within the body which is already overheated, and causes fever to come.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it needs to be drained of a great quantity, and the opening [of the vein] is widened so that it can reach up to the shoulder.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you correct all the surgeon's conditions, and put your hand on his pulse when he is suturing, so that death does not come instead of recovery, and this happens many times, when the surgeon is neglectful.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary when you see that the arm comes loose, and blood issues again the second time, and the opening [of the vein] is closed, that you press heavily upon it.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If he is bent, let him straighten out his arm quickly, for it would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let him leave it alone until it heals the second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you should insert the tip of the flame until the blood that has congealed into a lump at the opening of the vein begins to flow, and put on a poultice made with water and press on it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the abscess is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the swelling has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to let out blood the second time, then he heals in that same place, or in another abscess, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The wound on the arm is healed in place of the swelling of the head because it was composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is that the patient puts his hand into hot water until the scab is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then bind it moderately, so that the vein appears well, and now heal him through the middle, not from the side nor from the length;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the puncture should be wide, and he should be healed well near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot issue from it, then put his hand in hot water, and let the blood run into the water as much as you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is in summer, then do not rub the hand with hot water, for you will put it more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the vein of this wound is safer from all other wounds, for there are no artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the palm of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	bind the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein shows itself, if one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein is across, and you clip it entirely from top to bottom, then nothing will hurt.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go too deep, for the nerves are under all naked of flesh, and then put the hand in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the wound with oil as long as it is needed, then put a compress on the abscess to close it quickly, and do this for each pain. (Note: "hastanment" means "quickly", and "chescun rain" is an archaic way of saying "each time")
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The cure for the abscess in the left hand is worth for the disease of the spleen, and do everything similarly as I told you about the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the spleen is valuable for all diseases that are under the body, such as illnesses of the liver, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of his health is such that the patient puts his foot in hot water and scrapes on the vein as long as it hurts, and binds over the joint of the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there goes much blood dripping;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	cure then where the largest vein flows, or at the ankle, which is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you cure it above the foot, take care of the nerves that are underneath, and the cure will also cross as in cutting;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the fomes be insensible.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the pus cannot come out, then put the foot in water again, and let it drain well from the abscess.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the surgeon fails the first time, then begin again the second time above a poultice, for the wound is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt of nerve, as we have said, and thus do the same for the soles of the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The sore of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the back leg, and its cure is worth for the pain in the hip, when it's due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his blood is such that the patient should enter into a bath, and strain on top of the ankle 3 to 4 times by twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then let the blood flow in all ways that you can, and across;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	it is worthwhile to take out as much as possible, for the place is clean, and it has been gathered back in the hands of many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then let blood flow from the vein that opens at the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and do so much letting out of blood as you see fit, and then loosen the tie, and put on a cloth and tighten.
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	bloodlettings with a bellows (or possibly "with suction")
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Venesections are made of horns, or iron, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and purging is done in two manners:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this purging which is done without piercing is in two manners:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is all fire, or not fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and purging which is done by piercing and extraction of blood is made in 14 places of the body, for one of which is all on the head itself;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in both sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the siphon under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the siphons on both shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the siphons above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the siphons in both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the siphons in both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cupping of both ankles.
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and cupping does not treat blood loss, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it has no effect at all, just like we make a cut to let out blood.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it does not need to be administered, nor with any fire, or sense of fire, in any disease that comes from being over-full, as long as all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if through necessity of disease it is necessary to cup, or because of habit, then let us administer each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between, and each time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are such people who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are such people who find fullness and redness in their face, and on their head, and in their neck, and darkness around their eyes.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and bleed.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are such people who think, and see by the blood and wounds and deaths and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and just the same when it's in the month, we order them to be ventoused after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sinus of the nose is so helpful to the headache... that comes to the eyes, and it does not need to be after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this vomiting is in place of the sinus of the brain, and it does not need that those who are of cold complexion make use of it, or who have catarrh, for it causes them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not necessary that the elderly make use of it, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who cure themselves with it often become forgetful, and for this reason the ventouse should be placed a bit lower by the back of the head, in order to counteract forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The vomiting in the throat is in place of the sinus of the head and of the vertebrae, and because of that it is worth it for the constriction of the belly, and for the fissure of the channel of the womb, and for all these things.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it must be pressed firmly, for if it holds too tightly, it causes obstruction of the bowels or stomach and of the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventoses of the two costal arteries beneath the neck are worth the pains in the head, and obtalmia and emigration, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is a sign of the disease of the Basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and you must instruct the surgeon to extend his hand to place it, that he not cut the artery and do not come away with excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The ventoses under the chin are worth for the disease of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is a sign of the bleedings from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventousation on the shoulders is worth for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The ventoses on the sides are worth as much as three veins of the arm, because they drain blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the surgeon that he shall not cut too deep, for the place is bare of flesh and lies beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The poultice that is on the backside is useful for purging from the fundament and for diseases underneath; and it must be large, and of lead, so that it can draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and perhaps if it were too fine, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The poultices of the legs clearly heal them, because they draw blood from all the body, and are worth for ancient pains in the groin, and in the kidneys, and in the bladder, and they break the boils.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are in place of the two soles and the two ankles; and nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and cause pallor in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner of applying the bellows is such that you should first put it empty and then temper it; and quickly put it in place, and move evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see the red color and swelling, and observe the reddening due to blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then heat it up, and put on the bandages again, and observe in the condition of the body, for there are some who have thick flesh, and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	it is necessary to inflict a wound only once, and it is necessary to make wide incisions, and slightly deep ones.
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to inflict a wound twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time in order to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to inflict a wound a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw out a little bit of blood here and there, if it pours only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want to let out much blood, then we often recommence.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, then we cut in deep and the ends should be pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those with tough skin and hard flesh, and who have large pores, that you grease the places of the cupping glasses with astringent and dissolvent oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is with essence of violet, or oil of sweet almonds, or oil of cucumber seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is with olive oil, or oil of parsley, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, then take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person to whom we give treatment has soft skin and large pores, then there is no need to put a point of oil, but it should be washed after the poulticing with rose water, or cold water, or vervain water, or cucumber seed water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, should rise from ashes, or wormwood water, and sumac, and similar things. (Note: "mout de moistor" likely means someone with a lot of bodily fluids or moisture)
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities rise from old wine, or water of marshmallow, or the decoction of wormwood or chamomile, or similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it does not seem necessary to heal with a ventouse before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and does not sleep at all after the ventouse and must be warned that when it needs to be ventosed and when it is ventosed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are healing themselves as being choleric, and whose blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so it is necessary for him to take cold things, such as green apples and endive and lettuce at mealtime, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and young pig, and kid meat, and moistened meats.
