Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, take honey syrup and moderately fragrant wine which is between old and new, and kid meat, and young pig, and small birds and chickens.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day when he will sweat profusely, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	it is necessary to give some men some time triple or muscatel wine before sweating, or afterwards, in order to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and draw out the blood, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The poultices that are put to hurt are those that are put above the liver, and above the spleen, and podagra, and above the belly and the navel and the loins and the hip, for these members do not suffer being hurt there, and it is only done in order to draw blood from member to member, as we put on the breasts when the nipple bleeds;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	in order to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put poultices on the belly and on the navel to reduce the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it takes away the pain, when there is an inflammation or stone, so that by its attractive virtue it takes away the inflammation, or dislodges the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus it also does when one applies it above the liver and above the spleen when there is retained windiness, and these cups are administered empty to suck out as much as possible;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and at any time they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot vinegar, such as in the disease of the tear-duct, and in this manner one fills the cup with hot vinegar alone, or with vinegar into which herbs have been steeped that are good for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the ventouse administered with fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	It must be two fingers in width and half a palm deep, and it should go on the side around the middle of the leg as if to push an awl, and it should be of tin, soft so that it does not harm the patient when placed on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And it has in its midst a rod of crossing iron or steel, to place a candle attached, and in them there are both great and small ones according to the illnesses and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of adults, and of the thin from the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And thus one must place this cupping glass above the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	light the candle with wax or ointment and place it in the cupping glass on top of the rod that is inside the cupping glass, so that the light be at the bottom of the cupping glass, that it not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it above the member, and you should be above the hole that we have said, so that when one wants to, the steam goes out, and remove the cupping glass;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and light another ointment as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the syringe which is administered in illness of dropsy, all acute, has no rod nor pore, and is not ministered before it is full of water, and is placed on the member only so much;
et c’est li forme:	and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sponges are not ministered before places where you cannot put syringes because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare places of skin, such as elbows or knees, and other similar ones;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of this sponge is that when you find sponges which are in sweet clean water without pores, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them into a nut in sweet clear water, until they are well known and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be bled from vein and syringe, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the sponges;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are smooth and red, and healthy-looking, then it is in a place where one can put a bloodletting cup, so if you put it there, because it is very beneficial afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the place from above, and then from below, carefully, and then compress it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place becomes too sore later on the body of the abscesses, then moisten a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the swelling is stilled.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the swelling is multiplied, then put on verdigre ash or gall, and similar things, until it is stilled.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the place half of split peas, and leave them there until they burn at the place, it will be stilled now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, then take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the scabs do not want to come off, then rub the place with fresh blood; or you put a needle in it until the pus comes out, and then put them on; and as soon as they feel the blood, they will heal.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are suppurating, then sprinkle on a little aloes and linseed powder, or ash, so they will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	The book of wounds begins here. (Note: this likely marks the end of the section on ventouses and the beginning of a new chapter in the medical text)
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a treatment for wounds and swellings.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Learn, young son, that the foolish men turn away from this chapter, who never saw a single one of the ancient books, nor read a letter among them;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of that reason the art is estranged in our land, for I never found any good ones.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing else, except by the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated their science and by experience, and by the habituation of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And I have already described in this chapter what is contained, and summarized at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are brought, as I have done in these two chapters preceding.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say the prologue of this book, which contains the sum of words and chapters where the wise man sets his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are proven know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a break or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary for you to hasten and cure the patient first, on one hand; and if any other thing does not prevent you, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is very cold, or too hot;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and if he has a chill from cold juices, that is to say, cold joints and meat of bird and goat and does not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and does not fill himself too much with meats which fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of hot abscess or spreading of matter in the member.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient recovers from their previous main treatment then they are to be instructed.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone starts to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make thick nourishment, or have viscosity, such as boiled wheat, rice, cheese, and veal, and eggs, and fresh fish, and rich wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with proper nourishment the bone heals more quickly and sooner the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of old men and decrepit people cannot be well recovered or healed according to their nature because of the fragility of the members, nor those who are too soft, such as children's bones.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no treatment, remove the broken bone with large splints that are thick and join the member together, so that it becomes strong as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not put all his strength back into him, and because of this he must be fed on thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breakages are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the breakage of the head is different from the breakage of the thigh or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that bend (or fracture) at a curve, and others in a crackling manner, such as the breakage of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And also a break with an open wound, and a break with a small crack or fissure throughout its entire length.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in each manner he should have his own device and proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory brings him back to its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the break of the bone is known by what it is twisted and open well from behind, and resounds under the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or spraining of the shoulder, and the patient feels little pain, then there is no break.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can still have a twist, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you should not move the hand at all, but put on medications that come next, and then bind it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaks that come together in a circle, and are the two parts dislocated, you must now put them back to an equal point, so that the swelling comes.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the swelling comes, let him leave it alone for a day, until the swelling is calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then place it in its natural position with the help of an assistant who can lift it lightly and gently, and know that the restoration of the joint is easier than the restorations of those where there are fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold it in place, as should be done afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and it is two parts, whether it is an arm or foot, or with your hand it is small members, or with two cords, or with one cord and with your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member back in its natural shape; so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, then fix all the adhesions in their places with all possible means as quickly as you can, and take care that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and set the two joints of the bones back together in the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And have it felt by hand if you think it is not well.
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if it sets well and is not strained too much or pressed as those do who bring about abscess hot and contractions in the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is at the right point, then scold the patient so that he does not move it, neither in waking nor in sleeping, nor in turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the limb is so secure that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, it is not at all; and he must be put in such condition that he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and that he be kept straight, so that there is no twisting when he is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small members, such as bones and tendons and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is necessary to envelop a cloth of soft and subtle linen.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are thick, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is necessary to envelop with a wide and hard linen, for the wide linens encircle the entire large member, and hold it in place evenly from all parts, so that there is no looseness.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie on lightweight bandages, three turns or four according to the member, and hold with your hand one stick at the entire linen, then go above the break and bind it less tightly, so that the break is a little distant from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the ligament little by little, as long as you take a great part of the true place, then take up the other ligament and turn it back around on the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the break and hold it moderately, not too hard nor too gently, as we have said in the first line above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the ligaments strips of linen or cloth, as long as it is entirely even, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, then put on something soothing and warm for the abscess and which takes away the swelling, and leave it thus for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then hold onto the splints and let them be of the thickness of a well-filled cane or of wood from which one makes wedges, or of palm shoots, and be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the staple that one puts on the breakage be a little thicker and larger than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be also as long as is necessary for the member of smallness or greatness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind up on the staples in the same way that you did at the first joint, then tie above with a thread appropriately, just as above the breakage;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter is above, then less;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be middle, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of fine linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, as those of the fools who make their bonds with linen cords twisted wrong, and it is a great error, for the bandage cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it should not have between each staple less than two inches of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the splints after they are tightened in their proper place, then put underneath them linen cloths or lint to prevent bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break and the ligament is broken, I will say how it should be cured later on.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that you must not bind with splints all the broken members at first.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For since the member is large, one must not apply a cauterization too soon, but rather after nine days or seven, or more depending on the safety of an abscess forming nearby.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and behold here is the manner of ancient ointments for restoring breakage, dislocation, and twisting:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that remains at the sides of the mill, and mix it with abundant egg, and put this concoction, neither too clear nor too thick, to use it, and this is the common manner of the ointment restoring breakage in many dispositions, and similarly for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another manner of ointment restoring breakage and dislocation and twisting:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	take 3 absinthes and danium and myrrh and asafoetida and gum arabic and mastic, ten parts of it.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Myrrh and aloe, of which one takes five parts;
alechil VIIII З.;	Aloe nine parts;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into powder, and mix with almond oil;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the complexion of the man is hot, then use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another manner of plaster that is good for twisting;
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take myrrh and sweet valerian, ten parts;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Myrrh and aloe, nine parts;
acaice VI З.;	Acaica six parts;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Take Armenian balsam ten parts, and grind it well, and mix with vinegar or almond oil, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another manner of plaster for joints and bones that have been separated from their places, and quiets the pain beforehand, and the fracture; they use the bone, and the breakage:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new linen cloth, and smear it with fresh mint and cooked oil, and place it on the location.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore [it], but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and properly removing the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another manner of plaster that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and dry earth leaves, and crush them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of plastering for the restoration of the breakage of the bone and to reduce the remaining part of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take the root of wormwood, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour from each one in equal parts;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and crush them, and mix with wine, and if the member is heated, mix with moisted water of coriander or with water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of poultice more intense than the first, when a hard abscess comes to restoring the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take the roots of wormwood and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, sage, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and crush them, and mix with salt water or sweet water or with wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that when restoring a broken member, one should only apply ointment made of wax and oil on it, and nothing else, and that it should be between two extremes, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that when restoring a broken member, one should apply dry and slightly warm things on it, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, which we have already mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another manner of plugging that is good for lesions and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take marigold and hemp of the field, or feathers of birds, and wormwood, and mix them equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then the dislocation will loosen after a little while, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved out of its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if it is not loosened by hands the next day.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, or swelling, without rest or decrease, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and lift the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry lint, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it with a knot, until you are sure of warm swelling;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and let the inflammation of the member rest, and may it be removed from pain; then resume the subtle binding, and a poultice, and do not bind it so tightly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess and redness and pain and swelling have completely gone away, and you need to continue with poultice and bandage, then start again as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the member, do not untie it until after three days or four or five or seven;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and any time let it be twenty days, according to what we see, until the crack is closed, and the joint approaches the flesh on top.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then bind it tighter than before, and the swelling increases in its flesh, as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the place drying out more than necessary is, know that inflammation cannot come;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	apply hot oil to the joint then every third day and anoint it with a little vinegar;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	through this work then cuts the inflammation from the member and straightens it quickly what foolish practitioners do who leave the member twisted;
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is bad and fearful work and I see nothing else but to cut loose and do it properly;
des diverses manieres de brisure	It seems like the text is concluding with a heading "des diverses manieres de brisure", which translates to "of various manners of breakage" or "of different types of fractures". This suggests that the author is about to discuss or describe various types of breaks or injuries, possibly in preparation for discussing treatment methods.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breaks and diverse shapes and the causes are assigned;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are breaks that are caused by the strike of a sword and the elbow crushes all the bone right up to the sifac which is under the bone just as an axe or club does;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and therefore this manner of breaking is called "hacheure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the spear hits the bone above without piercing, and it is called this manner of breaking "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and it is the wound from these two breakings great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it's a crushing blow, or a splitting break, or from the back of the arm with stone, or falling on stone, or other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it's a comminuted break, which approaches just to the periosteum that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is closed in the bone as subtle as a thread, and it is a small crack, and because of this it is called this break "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made either by striking with stone or by falling or by something similar and makes the bone's splinter go downwards and it forms a cavity so that as boilermakers do when they heat up the cauldrons.
si entre li piere dedens.	if stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this occurs more often in those who have wet bones in the head, such as an infant's skull.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and there occurs to all these types of breakage where small pieces are separated as if they were.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all manners of breaks by the signs on them, and the investigation that is made, and by the corrupt flesh that is over them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary break is known by the fact that when one discovers the bone and rubs it gently, the break opens up black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a break, be careful about accidents that can occur in the patient. And if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, swelling, and fever ague, or if they persist and become red, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it cannot be healed with any doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident and you hope for recovery, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes first to you, and it's in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon that you can see.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the periosteum under the bone is not corrupted and the accidents we mentioned come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the break of the bone comes right up to the skin that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part like this:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and take the head of the patient wounded, and uncover above the bone in every way that you can, and on the shape of the wound as soft as you can, and if the bleeding of blood comes to reveal the bone, or an abscess forms, then the help of those things that are needed, and it is that you fill the place with damp cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the abscess is calmed down, and be sure that the bleeding of blood has stopped.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begins around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two manners of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one manner is that you chisel with a narrow tool in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put another tool, larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have a number of various chisels, some narrow and others wide, and pointed, and made of hard iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly, so that you do not bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and strong, then you should make holes around it, so that you administer chisels with handles, not too deep lest they pierce through to the marrow of the bone, and above the point there must be a margin or circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have several of them, so that each one comes to its place within the thickness of the bone, so that you have handles for all the tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the shape of the three ways of burning (or cauterizing):
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one cauterizer on the bone, and turn to your back so that you know the bone has been pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then put the cauterizer somewhere else a little while later, and so do this all around, then take out the incisors the space of the bone that is between the portholes, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw out the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as tongs, forceps;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and be careful not to touch the brain nor the spleen.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you reset the apertet which remains of the bone to all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it must be more rigid and more subtle than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	If he remains nothing of small bones, or any scales, then loosen the bone with gentle instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then heal the wound with tents and unguents as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other manner of working which is that which Galien says, which is more sure.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and hold him very firmly, and it is his command.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone, at the place where the fracture is most apparent, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will put under the head of this lancet a lens-shaped thing:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, and if the parts are uneven on both sides, then the cutting should be towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then tap with a small mallet upwards, so that you lightly chisel the bone all around, and be careful of the thread that is underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it adheres to the bone, then loosen it lightly, for one loosens it very harmlessly and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce up to the cloth, and the bone is chipped only on top, and there are small pieces, then you should scrape off that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine scraper which you should have various quantities of, so as to adjust in each place what is most convenient, according to the work and figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you pass before coarse scrapers, and then more fine ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other cauterizations and subtle breaks, it is necessary that you apply a cause according to its direction.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that is not returned to him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the suppurative flux is uncovered, you should take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and wet it in rose oil, and put it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another double cloth of linen in two or three layers, and wet it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as lightly as you can so that you do not irritate the suppurative flux, then administer over the other linen, and do not press it too hard until it merely touches the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it be thus for one or two days until the swelling of the abscess is calmed, then loosen it and administer medicine such as lily roots, and vetch flour, and frankincense powder, and theriac, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make powder from these things, and put it on the wound, and administer various medicines without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and take care that the wound is kept clean, and do not leave any ointment there, nor allow any threads to be sewn on it, because when the threads gather on the skin of the brain, they irritate and rot, and cause great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one puts a caustic thing on the eye, it necrotizes above it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Be on guard then, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if there is no purging that comes from the medicine one has put on it, so that such a virtue may be, then you must take part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them together with one cloth to make a poultice, and put it on the eye.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound in the ways of treatments that are necessary until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes are broken the two parts of the neck above, or one by the separation, for they are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and that one below is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is crushed or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must apply your little finger or perforation to the neck, and place that breakage inside your middle finger, and at the end, so long as the neck returns to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.

And if the break is in the upper part of the bone and it cannot be set straight, then you should put a stick or a small rod into the head of the bone to support it.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the breakage is of two parts, then do it in the same way, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not then after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then bind a cloth at the top of the neck with a bandage made of linen, if the breakage is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Where you push one side against the other, if there is a break on this side.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the tents be so large that they fill the openings of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said a certain physician that one must wash the tents with lard, and move each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it should be that they are moistened with a mixture of marrow of egg and miller's powder.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the tent, until the bone is hardened and the cartilage has become firm.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And at no time push in into the nose feathers of goose in place of tents, and if it has a soft wrapping around it, and keeps the breakage steady, and the patient breathes through.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or make the gauze that you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if a swelling comes to the bone while you are working on it, then put a poultice of melted wax or cotton in rose oil, or in a small quantity of aquilantum (a type of ointment) onto it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscess does not come out, apply an ointment behind it, of barley flour and incense powder mixed with egg marrow, then put on light poultices, and do not tie the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break of the bone is small and it is broken into little pieces, then take out the fragments with suitable instruments for this; then fill the crack, and treat things that come loose with meat, and soldering, as plasters and ointments suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the bone, then treat it with tents and put in poultices of lint until they are healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	It seems we've moved on to a new topic.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured below and there is no wound outside, and the breakage is only outward, and it is not split in two, but rather hollow inside, one recognizes this lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the break is on the right side, that you poke your index finger into the mouth of the patient.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the break is on the left jaw, then poke your index finger of the right hand into it lightly, and hold it even with the other hand by force.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is split into two, it is necessary that you provide an extension of 1/2 part on each side, so that it becomes even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement of the teeth causes or bruising, then hold them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jaw grease and put on a double cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and put on the flag (or) a great bandage well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it up at your discretion that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and serve light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the face changes, untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a plaster on it, of mill dust with abundance of egg or sesame flour after you have removed the wax.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and apply a linen plaster lightly, and if the plaster has hardened, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until they are healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	it is often healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess or swelling comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a break and wound together, repair the first part of the bone that was taken out;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if subtlety of removing with suitable instruments is recommended to those who.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with fire as needed according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, close the wound, if it is wide, and put on one or two ointments suitable to this, to prevent pus, until they are healed.
de la forcele	of strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The collarbone breaks in front more than once near the shoulder, and the break occurs in three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and separated into two, with pieces, and it is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is break with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is such that when there is break without wound, you have two attendants, so that one holds the shoulder where the collarbone is broken;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other stretches out the neck towards the part.
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then place equal the break to your chest, so that the shape is such as it should be, and there will be no appearance or unevenness.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to stretch it further, place under the shoulder on the patient a rounded rod of cloth, or wool, and make it thick according to your necessity.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And then tie the tourniquet, and strain the point of the spear to your hand, so that you set it even on the break, as is necessary.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forcelet out to the front because it comes in depth, it is necessary that the patient lies on their side over their bed, and puts a bolster under their shoulder; and pushes the assistant's shoulder down, so that the bone of the forcelet is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then bring the break to your chest, and if you do not find any fragments, it is necessary that you split on top.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and pull out the broken pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join together by any sort of binding, then cut it with one of the knives that you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but put under the tourniquet this instrument, so as to protect the sinew.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and make it like a spoon, and it is not sharp, and should be as wide as is necessary according to the size of the bone and the power of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two handles, such as you see, and let one be wide and the other narrow, like the shape of the wound that you made when you pulled out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are assured of a hot abscess, if the wound smells, and if the ulcer is small, or you doubt the abscess is hot, employ the wound with cloth and tents according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot inflammation comes, wet one cloth in rose oil, garlic, and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The splinting of the bone, when it is with open wounds and incisions, is that you put on the bone a poultice of flour and egg yolk paste, and put light stoppings over, and put a spear under the splint, if you need it.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very long band of a palm in width, then put the doubled cloth on top of the stoppings and the poultice.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a thin staff of three inches in width and length, and wind it around the bandaged part, so that the ends of the bandage are hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and put the steel on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the sound saddle, and under the sick saddle;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and the reset of each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the steel does not move over the broken bone, then secure it every day, and when the ligature loosens, then hold it;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient sit on a backrest, and put him when he sleeps a small bolster under the saddle, to lift the shoulder up;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	so the fracture of the collarbone will be alleviated by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it until bad accidents may come, up to twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then renew the plaster, if you see that it is necessary, and hold (the shoulder) in place and leave it so, until it be restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and she is restored to health in twenty-eight days, and in less time to some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	A break occurs when the shoulder blade is dislocated or its place is made wide, and it cannot be known if it is sound except by feeling with one's hands;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if the apparatus is set according to the shape of the break, and it is reset according to its natural form, in all ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put powder of the mill with abundance of egg on it, and light cloths, and place a folded cloth over it;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place a long and subtle splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and under the splint are thongs in any part of the shoulder, if you fill those threads with linen cloths, so that the splint sits evenly;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then bind it with a strong band tightly, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the knot every day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time he dislocates, if he holds steady, and places the arm equal to its place, and puts the patient on his side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is recovered in 20 days or in 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is completed, if it dislocates again, and be careful, for it is not bone that becomes loose lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone sticks out and points over the skin, then make a poultice on it, and apply an ointment, and do what we said to soothe a boil. (Note: The text is likely referring to a technique for managing a bone infection or abscess, where a poultice and ointment are used to draw out the infection.)
de la brisure dou pis	C'est le début de l'article ! "De la brisure du pis" est un titre qui suggère que l'article va traiter d'une blessure ou d'une rupture au sein (le "pis" désignant probablement le sein, mais peut aussi faire référence à une blessure à la poitrine).
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bones are sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, has swelling, heat, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the sinews in the broken bone, and senses its presence.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back, and puts an I-cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and gathers together the ribs of the two costal bones with your hands, and carefully do what is needed to put them equal in every way that you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then put on plasters and bandages above the sharp star-shaped steel instrument made of salt or another light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the bandage back to the back, and hold it securely, and every hour make sure it is loose again, and if it becomes tight, then tighten it.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to untie it, due to corrosion or itching that comes from the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten and untie it, and scrape off the plaster, and address what has come out in the manner of treatments.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then re-tighten the bandage, and hold it tight until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Il semble que nous ayons une partie de l'ouvrage "La Chirurgie" d'Alphonse de Hautenville, un médecin du Moyen Âge.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not occur unless in large places after the back, and in the head within, and they do not bend except because they are slippery.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and he knows well at the examination what to do.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedy is that you place it evenly over the break, as it needs to be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply a poultice and tie with an iron band, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the break of the ribs is declining inward, then the patient feels very great pain and puncture, also like weeping, because the bone pierces the membrane.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and he is wounded by needles, and burns and vomits great abundance of blood, and it is a grave sickness, and the ancients have put great remedy.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, in order to drive the breakage outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot abscesses come to it, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, let them heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they said that one puts cupping glasses on the place to suck strongly, and it seems a good reason;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	nevertheless, there is doubt that the cupping glasses may attract the superfluities to the place because of the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And one of us said that the spot should be covered with moist wool in hot oil, and you put tents between the ribs to put back in its place the hollow part around it, then take care of the treatment for pleurisy, meat, and medication.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot suffer by the bone which pierces the membrane, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to incise above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath to protect the spleen.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then you must saw through the bone, and draw it slightly, and then sew shut the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and heal it with plasters, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if an abscess bursts forth, apply a damp cloth soaked in rose oil on top of it; and lay on the place.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal meanwhile the skin over what it concerns the abscess, and bind it tightly on top of the adjacent part where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a breakage occurs at the base of the broken bone, and there comes a time when it begins to bend;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone and you want to know if they will be healed or not, look closely at whether you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and unable to move or stretch, and when you prick them with a needle, feel no sensation.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that in many conditions it is mortal, and if they move and feel well when restrained and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient has been cured, if one puts treatment there.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you wish to know whether it is healed or not, see if the vertebrae are softened, and if the accident has left behind those things which are in their hands, and on the back there comes windiness and vomiting without will.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one has sown it on his stomach, such vomiting occurs without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is seated on his back and wants to sit, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if he does not take great care in his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to them, then the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that you apply warm poultice to it if there is a hot abscess; place on the spine oil of roses or oil from egg yolk until it is eased.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then apply one of the comforting and drying ointments to it, and bind it with a cloth, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if some bone breaks apart, you must cover it with a splint;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and break the bone, then sew together the two lips of the wound if it is large, with a seam, and treat him with ointment infusing fat meat until he is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the shoulder", put your pouch in your left hand and place it equal to the other hand at your power, then apply the poultice and the stake on top, if you need them;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then bind it, and if there is splintered bone, do the same on top, and scrape, and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	The break of the bone of the hip.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	There occurs rarely that the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it happens, there is little harm to the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and make it two long [inches], and bend towards the parting [of the thigh], and come to the patient's pain in the place, and pierce, and inflame what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you stretch your hand up, as high as you are above the breakage;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know what a fracture and deformity are;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is in the head alone, place it even so that the break forms into its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is two long, or it declines inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, as long as you see a restoration of that breakage appearing.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have placed it even, put on the poultice, then put on a splint of wood or of horn, and hold the break in place so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and dress the area below the ribs, until the flesh is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their sound side or on their back.
