Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a swelling appears there, do not touch it, until the swelling is calmed down, and put on what we have said before.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to restoring it, and hold it in place as is necessary, if there is no bad accident.
et c’est li maniere.	that is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The break of the arm.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is what is between the armpit and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two manners:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	take one straight branch of a hazel tree, larger than the finger.
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie it between two sticks, and lift them up, and place the patient on the saddle.
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then throw the broken arm above the branch so that it reaches the fulcrum, and have on middle a wooden fork, then lift up onto any heavy thing or the servant stretches below.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then place the patient's broken arm equal to his hands together, so that the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that you bind the patient on their bed, and tie their hand to their neck, then command two attendants that one binds what is above the breakage with bandages to their hands, and the other binds underneath each strip, and stretch both of them to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then hold fast to the thread under the bandage and on the bandage, and stretch each of the ministers to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is near the top of the shoulder blade, then it is fitting that you place the middle strap under the saddle and the other towards the armpit, under the break.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the break is towards the armpit, then it is fitting to put the strap slightly, without force, so that the break is even above the place and on the armpit.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then put equal the breakage, as it is fitting, and hold tight; if an abscess grows there, it will not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess grows there, do not hold tight for seven days, and put on a linen cloth soaked in rose oil and vinegar until the abscess is appeased.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then hold tight, and the manner of holding tight is that you put on the plaster above the breakage, then bring the arm back onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put on the bandage, and hold tight on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place of rest, if nothing prevents it or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone is not moved, use splints, and put on the breakage a wider and stronger splint than the others, and have between each splint two spaces, and let each splint be as long so it passes over the breakage three fingers in from either side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then bind it up tightly, just like I said at the beginning of this chapter about breaking, but stronger and not so loose.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the setting of the stars, and the binding, just like we have said, in the time that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the warm abscess, so leave it to bind until the seventh day, just like we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then look at it every three days the binding, that it does not become inflamed or swollen, or there come to the member redness because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it heals, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents come to it, do not loosen the binding until after three days or more, and the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put under the shoulder one cushion plump with wool evenly, and look every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken member does not move, or the binding be loosened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If the patient is cured by the virtue of medicine, and he is given meat that we have previously mentioned, in such a manner that the meat is at the first subtleties.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to recover, it will be large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset in forty days from the start;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must untie it and administer bath and ointments of medicaments to set the place right.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and tightened, one should not dislodge it for 7 days or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	It looks like we've reached the end of the text about treating a broken arm.
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "two fosciles", one of which is small, and that is the one which joins the elbow.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is that one which is underneath, towards the small bone;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	perhaps only the great bone breaks, or the little one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bones are broken, restoration is easy, and healing.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large ones are broken, it is a bad healing, and more painful than when they were broken in two together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then one should lightly extend it and set it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if that's the great bone, then you must strain it more firmly;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and stretch it up above the chest, and raise the elbow of the hand higher than the others, and the small bones lower than the others, and let the patient cross over on himself, and have his hands in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any work.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then stretch out the minister's arm to the part below his hand, or to the joint, and another minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the glass equal, according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break there are fragments, then place each one in its proper position, and if there is any that cannot be grasped by forceps, and you can't restore it to its place, then send for a surgeon, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the break it makes an open wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	Take care of oneself.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration there arise abscesses, then apply a cloth made from rose oil and white wax, which is not too hard or too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and bind the cloth on top gently, until the hot abscesses are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the wax and put on a poultice made from mill powder with an abundance of egg whites; then apply plasters, and let the plaster of the breakage be at once stronger, and a little bit larger than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that he must have six arm or splint arrangements in more positions.
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the breakage is in one of the bones, or in two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and strain more upwards on the breakage than anywhere else, and always less while loosening, as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the dressings that are on the fresh wound be soft and moist, and not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and the thread, from which it is strained, should be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if some evil accident comes to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then it is necessary to bathe the member in hot water, until those itchings are appeased;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the member rest and not be cramped.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then start to bind it again; and if the joint is softened and the bone separated, and similar thing, address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that the stiffness cannot come to the member, because it is too narrow, so it is necessary that you soften it a little, and then let it be for some days, until the stiffness goes away, and then strain it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not loosen the bandage until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or ask him to turn around, then lie on his back and have his hands behind his neck, and let his necks be even, and beware of movement and disturbance, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this wound is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and humoral conditions of the patient.
de la brisure de la main	Il semble que nous avons changé de sujet ! Nous étions en train de parler d'une briseure du membre (bras ou jambe), et maintenant il semble que nous passons à une briseure de la main.
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and at the wrists there are small breaks, and it only rains many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary for the patient to sit cross-legged, and sit upright before him evenly.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then place his hand on the stretched cloth and stretch out the attendants who have broken bones, and put the broken ones level with each other in sight, until they are well aligned.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply an ointment and a poultice to it, so that the abscess does not come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the break.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be wrapped up in an "I" shape of linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the break is on the side around the stomach of the hand, make a sphere of linen cloth and instruct the patient to press it against his broken hand.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then strain it with a long cloth, and the splint should be of good wood as big as the hand, and strain it, as is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the end, it's necessary that you put a splint on top, and another underneath in the wrist, so that the hand is open and straight; then tie all around the hand, and bind the bandage between the wrists.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	If the splint comes to any of us from below the shoulders, if it is the arm, then he sets it even, as it should;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and holds it with the sole, and if you see that he sets a straight little stick to lift the splint, and does not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the break is in other joints, such as in the finger or one of the others, then he sets it even and ties with a sound ligature which is behind;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you bind them all together in one holding, as much as it's worth, or put a splint on top of them, just like the arm;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in restoration and arrangement of a warm abscess, and close up those that come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Il semble que nous sommes en train de lire un texte médical ancien, probablement du Moyen Âge. Les instructions pour le soin des blessures et fractures sont écrites d'une manière qui rappelle les traités médicaux médiévaux.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the thigh is many times broken, and it can be well seen when it turns forward and backward;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is to tie him up with a bandage above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his back, then stretches each of his limbs to an equal length.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and that is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the thigh, then it will be one of the tendons towards the armpit, and the other ligaments below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, and then let the bandage be below the knee, and let the extension be downward.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then put the splint on the bone equally to both hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then put the poultice and the bandage, if an abscess does not come from it.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it cool down first then return to your work and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	the linen bandage is made in the same way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap above the break with a hard linen cloth doubled in two or three, and leaving the superfluous parts, then turn the leg so that the toes come to the root of the kneecap, and tie a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the thread up.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn up the leg and crotch to bandage; then put on a splint above the break; and put a splint on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then place the soft cloth or wool in the middle between the leg and crotch to put even pressure; then begin to bind strongly three turns or four above the break.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go higher up from the break, the tension should be less.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then take the two ends of the thread that you have placed between the leg and crotch, and bind three stitches above; then go back down to the bottom end of the thread, as far as near the foot.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and bind it so that it doesn't move from its place; then leave it thus, and if there is no swelling, abscess or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	If it happens, then loosen it and straighten what is out of place, as we have said many times.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are fragments of bone that grasp, then it must be cleaned up, if one can;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, then the place must be split open and the fragment drawn out;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and heal it as we have said, until they are sound.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And once the scrotum is broken in such a way that stars are put into it, as in the aid and the arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	nevertheless, in the restoration thus made does not shatter the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And you know that the skin is restored in 7 days, or a little more or a little less, according to the diversity of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the gouty armpit
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that there is often a small fracture, but it folds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then it's just a split or a hole, and there is a wound in every case, and without a wound, and this seems to be true.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is such that one sets even what is broken at its shoulders, as long as it can be assembled.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then put a poultice on it, and place a rounded star on it if you need to, and tie it as is fitting, then follow all the arrangements that we have said for other breakings, such as a hot abscess and similar things;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he puts himself in every accident from which it behooves him, as long as he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of a broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, from which one is called by right not "tibia", and the other is called "fibula".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And there is just as much breaking of it like when it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is similar to that of the arm equally, and the works are all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg twists from all parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fibula (subtilz) is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, then one feels great pain, and it can be seen well;
et torne desoz.	and turns greenish.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then administer an extension, and put it even, and tie the splints equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but always, if the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and perform it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have finished your work, take two wooden splints that go around the leg on both sides, and are as long as from the knee to below.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap two thicknesses of bandage over and under it, and tie them together in the middle, so that at this time the leg cannot lean to the right or to the left, and thus it is well.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and some administer two splints as long as the leg, and they are made of wood, and one places the leg to prevent movement, and this is properly done in the break or wound.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and each day move the leg around, to see if there is an abscess or other accident.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if it cures until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of a broken bone of the foot (or possibly "foot" rather than "piet", which could be a type of fruit)
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is rarely a break, but sometimes the bones of the foot break and become disjointed, and in more severe cases there may be crushing.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a fracture of the two bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping one another, have the patient place his foot on the ground as if he wanted to go, and then put now your foot on top of his, at that spot where the bones are raised, then press them so that they return to their places.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then put on the plaster and bandage above, and under the patient's belly of the foot a small board of two smooth edges, then bind it to the foot gently, then when you have wrapped the fabric around and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the splint, because you will find that the bones are equal, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there is any of the fingers broken, restore them, just as we have said for the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then put on the broken finger a splint according to the length of the finger and let it be one piece more thick, then place under the foot that small board which I have said, and bind it gently;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, break them; and put on each one a pin according to its quantity, wrapped in one cloth of linen, and hold the table under the foot.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and if they are on the head of the table outside the belly of the foot, so that it holds them well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other breakings, which we have spoken of;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and secure each accident as is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of a broken bone of the wrist (or possibly "poignil" is an old term for the wrist)
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of the natural fracture of the woman is broken, make her sit and stretch it out, then bend her towards the back part, and have it held by the back.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the natural cavity of the patient with cotton, and put in it as big a quantity as the fist.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then let the woman stand up and lift the back gently, then the cotton will pop out as far as it goes into the natural place, and the bone will return with the fist.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in and do so seven times or about:
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	so the break will be restored and if you see, take a bladder of heifers, and tie to the navel a cord, and put all the bladder in its natural place;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the cord strongly, until the bladder is inflated inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	nature will return the break;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then it should be filled with cotton and left like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the humerus of man or woman is broken, restore it thus as we have said in the femur;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these nearby breaks are not concealed from him who puts his study and skill into it, and listens to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture it signifies in many conditions the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	understand then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the thigh, when it is broken, take a goose girth and put the thigh in it;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then envelop him in cloth wrapped around, and let him be for three days or near to that, and he will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It behooves him who has a fracture with a wound, just as much if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or hip or similar one, that he be healed now, so that the stitches which we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but the splinter of glass remains, if you have nothing else, then start to restore the fracture in that very same hour, or on that day, so long as pus does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus comes, then leave the restoration just to the ninth day, so long as the pus is calmed down, and do not touch it on the tenth or quarter (day), for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the surface of the skin, it behooves you to put it in place lightly with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the splint is not prepared for you to put even with your hands, then straighten this instrument which is of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and the width according to the size of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and because of this it is necessary for the surgeon that he applies three or four, according to what is needed in each treatment of fracture;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and it should be curved and thick, so that it does not bend at the compression on the limb in your work, and should be angled in front, and thick in the middle in front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	It is called "palainche", because it is necessary to put a curved pin on top of the visible bone.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and the joint should be bound once, so that it may recover, and that they are even with one another.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then you must cut the top of the bone, as long as the instrument has purchase.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot put the bone back together, as we have said, then use a suitable tool, such as an instrument, or a knife, to your power.
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then reset those that are remaining in the bone with sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is replaced and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	So do as much to put it back in its place, then bind the joint with black vinegar dressing, and do it properly so that it is secure.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and put no cerote nor other thing on the wound with oil, lest it bring forth infection and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer bandages when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and bind the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted with the break.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times has this been done by foolish doctors, and they have had death or corruption brought upon the patient at least once;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and be the ligaments softer and more fragile than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accidents will come to it, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not necessary to put on unguents.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but envelop them entirely, in place of unguents, thick cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days the blood flowing from the wound, then remove what you have put on it of all vinegar, and apply salving ointment to healing wounds, such as quadruple remedy ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you bind the member two times a day, in the morning and at evening, until it be tightened and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the members be positioned in such a manner that the bowels hang downwards lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the member does not mend after many days and cannot tighten but instead becomes swollen, know that it has small pieces of bone, therefore it is necessary that you probe the wound with a tent, and remove all those unsound pieces that bring about this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter which precedes this one.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken, and it protrudes on the limb, as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar ones of the large members, do not pull it out, for many times death comes from this, but leave it alone until it rots.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	perhaps after 20 days or 30, something will come out of it afterwards, then cure the wound, if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot [do something], then let them [hairs] alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	sur les plaies qui s'ouvrent.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often see after the healing of a break, especially when it is near the joint, and that is an ugly sight for the shape of the member.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance cannot do the member its natural operations.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Then take care that the nose is fresh.
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if the administrator gives medicines that are styptics, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarsaparilla, aloe, and similar others, then thus take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with wine that is styptic, or with almond milk, or with oil.
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and place it on the nose in bandages, and bind it tightly, and do not loosen it until tomorrow morning.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then loosen it, and begin another one, until the swelling is gone.
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	When you bind over a well-made splint.
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of the splint is that it absorbs all swelling on the limbs.
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the lump has already turned to hardness like a stone, and it needs to be taken out, then cover it with a poultice, and make the excess come out.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you bind it tightly to any cloth until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	du membre qui est faible après la guérison.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the break in the bone is repaired, and remains behind the weak and fragile limbs, this occurs for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	because one is because it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been.
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many bandages, and the swelling could not come to the limb.
ou por multitude d’arosement;	due to a multiplicity of birthmarks;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of too great movements, not in its proper hour;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because he has little blood in his body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat and make the body tender, so that the blood be multiplied in him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer wine, and give him joy and cheerfulness;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then place ointment on the member, so that the ointment attracts to great inflammation, and cause it to rise often with great thickness, until the inflammation reaches the member;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	du membre tort après la guérison.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken apart, and the form of the member is ugly, nonetheless its natural operation does not fail.
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	Do not believe at all the fools who say one should break the member entirely anew; and many a foolish man has done this in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blamed, and great evils come from it, and perhaps the death ensues.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	nevertheless, if the swellings and tortures are fresh, it is necessary that they be raised with hot water, or that herbs which soften things be cooked, such as leaves of verbena, roots, and melilot, and similar things.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and the fay I softening plaster, such as well-made diacodium, and you take the root of verbena, and cook it with goose fat or oil of sassafras, and make a plaster on it.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you take fatty figs, and pound them with flaxseed of hemp, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by constant and prolonged rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And make gentle movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the dislocation is hardened and become like stone, and needs to be removed with iron, then it must be covered just up to the bone, lightly incised.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put a bandage and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Il semble que nous ayons atteint la fin du texte !
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur when a joint moves out of its place, because of which it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs again in anyone, if it needs to be put back into place now, it should now be restored to its natural position.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one waits, the swelling will grow, and it may happen that when you reset it, there are pain at the place.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	so it is not advisable to move it until it has deflated.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	it has brought forth many spasms and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient sweat, then let him go, until the swelling is eased.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as the cure will come back to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have written chapters on dislocations from the head to the hips.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	The lower jaw becomes loose, and the dislocation of both jaws is according to two manners.
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they are somewhat displaced from their places, and slightly softened.
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely loose and hang down towards the chest, and saliva drips from the mouth that he cannot hold it, nor can close his mouth, and enwraps his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it will return to its place by several applications.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must reset it quickly, and not tarry.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the attendants grasp the head of the patient, and insert the mirror's tip from one of their hands into the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands be outside to hold steady;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them on all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician puts it back into place, so that it returns to its natural position.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it is stubborn, especially if the two jaws together are stuck, then apply hot water and oil to loosen them gently.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not tug on the jaw, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back into place equally, and the patient's mouth is well moistened with a soothing ointment, then put on damp cloths soaked in rose oil and wax, and bind them lightly with soft strings.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient sleeps on his back, and their jaws are between two cushions, so that they do not move to the right or left, nor does he struggle to chew, but takes soft food, until the pains are gone, and the jaws are closed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then feed them lightly, and do not work at opening the mouth to eat and drink, until the jaw is well tightened and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not returned to their original position, then fevers and swelling will set in, and possibly diarrhea, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see these things, then know that they are bad omens.
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times death comes to him, within 9 days.
de la forcelle	...of the jaw. (The text appears to be an excerpt from an old medical manuscript, likely written in Middle French or Old French.)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation of the jaw cannot move away from the side towards the front, and it moves back only once, and one can feel it clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back, and extends their arms.
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press it firmly to your palm, and it will come back.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the plaster and the bandage, and bind him;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the shoulder that is near the collarbone cannot dislocate.
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it cannot be held in place and if it does dislodge at some time, then reset it to its place, as we have said.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then put on the poultice and the bandage, and hold it in place, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly bring back the head of the shoulder, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one of which is when it dislocates at the part below the armpit.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part around the chest;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and it dislocates above, and that happens frequently.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inward for the nerves.
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and many times dislocates downwards towards the armpit, exactly in those who have too much fat, for then it springs back strongly.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	those who have enough flesh, jump at pustules, and enter at pustules.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps happens to some men a blow or crushing, and inflames the shoulder with a hot swelling, and thinks it is dislocated by that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	it is necessary that you try it, until you are certain of the result;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known the dislocation when it falls toward the armpit, and makes a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among their diversity apparent.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and under the armpit against the chest the top of the shoulder, just as if it were an eagle.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand to their neck, nor move with any movement;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly against the chest.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this manner of dislocation is not other than to reset, when it is new, or if the infant is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the manner is that the attendant lifts the patient's hand up high, then places the thumbs under the elbow, and lifts the joint with great force up to its place;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the attendant lifts the hand and stretches it up high, then puts his hands underneath.
si venra hastanment.	then it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said within three days, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in warm water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the attendant brings soothing and calming, such as decoction of alea, and fennel, and marigold in water, and brings it;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then be covered the patient on his back, and place on under the elbow a strip of linen equal, not too soft nor too hard, then places the mirror at the heel above the strip, and lifts the head of the shoulder forcefully, and pulls the hand of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and one other attendant is to anoint the head of the patient, so that it does not move downwards;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	the shoulder returns immediately, and if you see it reset in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and that you cause a person to be present who is greater than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and straighten him towards the shoulder, and push his shoulder under the pillow of the patient, and lift up the pillow so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another attendant takes hold of the hand of the patient downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can hold onto something heavy, and the dislocation will now return.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And reset it also in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is that one puts a long iron rod into the earth, where the head is as hot as a spit, and not too large or too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it is put under the patient, but that it be wrapped soft above, and the patient feels the length of the wood;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then his hand is extended below on the other side forming, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return for all the things that we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a brand from the elbow of great size and four fingers wide, which has its tip rounded so it can easily enter deeply under the arm-pit, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then tie a cloth on the end of the staff so that it does not harm the patient, then place the staff under the arm-pit of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and stretch the staff of length above the elbow, and tie the aid on the staff, and the arm to the end of the hand, then place the arm on the shoulder of a wooden beam, and let the hands be extended below, and let the body hang from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint must now be reduced.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is reduced, however it may be, you should put under the elbow a staff of wool as tall; then place the poultice around with flour powder, with incense and egg oil, on all the shoulder and around, then the strain under the elbow properly, and turn the strap on the poultice, and embrace the hand to his neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he moves little by little, until the member is comforted, for it will heal more quickly.
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then move him more after 5 days or 7, and move him;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is firm and is not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come, or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cauterizations at three punctures, as they are described in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this and it dislocates after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is near the breast or shoulders, or back, is caused by force and stretching of arms, and one must administer another treatment;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let them heal until they are sound.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes grief to the member, and slowly in movement, the patient should bathe many times, until that grief is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	from a dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the shoulder joint is dislocated to points, and returns to points;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and if it has been completely dislocated, both in front and behind, and the dislocation is not restored, for one can see it well and feel it well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocate according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the cut of the sick person with the salt, so can you see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it so that suppurating swellings do not come, for if suppurating swellings came, it would be painful to reseat;
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance it cannot be reset entirely in its entirety, even when it is behind.
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	if it is worse than the other dislocations, and causes more great pain, and perhaps death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is such, when it can be reset in that way, that you stretch out its hand with both your hands.
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And his arm should be spread out, and the fingers to the mirror according to the cut around, over and under, and push the joint back into its sockets together, or to the root of his palm, so that it recovers to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and pushes with the root of his palm the shoulder which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong stretching;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and let two ministers stretch the arm, and hold it with both hands, so that it does not move from the stretching;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm to each side, then when you have enveloped a double long and wide cloth.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the mirror has joined the joint to his hand, then drive it away from any oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly, so that it recovers.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, then put on dry poultice with almond oil, and strain firmly, and support the arm to the neck of the patient, and let him for some days, then loosen.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, then loosen the ligament, and let it.
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then redo the poultice and the ligament, and let it like this for some days, until it is firmly set.
puis le deslie.	then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels pain after the return of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub him well, and press until it is relieved.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or you put a thick lamb's fat on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and let it enter into the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when he sweats, rub the joint temperately, then put the fat back on, and then enter into the bath.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and thus do it two or three times, until he is cured.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see this, put a poultice of warm moisted cow's flesh on it with butter, and bind it.
si revenra a sa disposition.	if it will come back to its place.
li dislocation de la main	It seems we've come full circle! The text appears to be a medieval medical treatise on how to treat a dislocated hand or wrist, specifically focusing on reduction techniques and aftercare.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and the return is light, more so than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to return it to its place promptly, in the same way that it was dislocated, and even if there is swelling or a hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the return is that you place the sick hand on a table, and extend the limbs of the hand, and have the fingers be equal, thus that it puts its palm on the appearance of the joint, and tighten it until it recovers.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	Nevertheless, you must see if it is well in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then put the patient's back of their hand on a table at extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient places their back on their hand on the table, and the physician places their hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it's well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	But if not, apply soothing plasters to abscesses, and let it be without starting again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot place it back in its proper position after some days, the dislocation remains twisted.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and does no harm to the patient as long as his hand is numb and cannot grasp anything at all.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then know that the nerves are bruised or the arteries.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	if there is no other remedy worse than to apply cauterization beside the wound, and perhaps it is not worth anything else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, he puts on the poultice that we have said, then tightens it and leaves it for 5 days, then loosens it and leaves it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he can't move it well and there's any stiffness, he soaks the hand in hot water, and rubs it until it is relaxed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	It seems that the text was about treating a specific medical condition, namely "dislocation of the thumb", which is an old-fashioned term for a type of joint injury or dislocation.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the joint of the hand is dislocated to each side, sometimes in the back of the palm or in the wrist.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then it is the joint, and push back the dislocation to its sockets until it returns, then support the head of the joint, and guide it towards the part where it was disjointed.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	And let him rest for two days, then make him even on that day.
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and bind it with a bandage as we have said, and loosen it the next day, and make him move it, and rebind it again.
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often until it is tight, and also do this if it is dislocated in the stomach of the hand, and do so as you have done before until it is healed.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and also do this when it is dislocated from the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from the dislocation of the vertebra of the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra of the back or of the neck is dislocated, or there are several that are dislocated, then there is no remedy, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are such that the evacuations jump out without will, nor can it be held, and many times they become soft in any member, or in both breasts or in two arms.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times the swelling moves to four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which moves to the back is called "gilbositas";
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The treatment for this is to return it to its place if the dislocation has come from infancy.
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no treatment or healing in sight at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or hitting or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment by great words say it does not bring much benefit.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the dislocation which comes to the shoulder in front, there is no remedy or healing.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes straight to both sides, and one cannot cure a bruise unless it is properly located in the back, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and that the patient be stretched out on his face in a straight place and have something to hold under him so that he does not get hurt.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then insert the stick into the ground nearby, and another one at the feet, and tie a string between the patient's knees, and another one to the thighs, and to the shanks, and to the ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two attendants know the strings, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two sticks;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well tightened, the stick as we have said, and the physician place his hands over the spine firmly, until it comes back.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this treatment, take a board three arm-lengths long, and hollow out the underside of it, and have the patient lie on their side, and place the head of the board under the skin, then put the middle of the board over the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and have the physician place their feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see, do it on the arm to which the tumor turns.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And you should place two torches on the head of the patient's arm, a large one and two smaller ones, with each torch having between them, above and below, an inch long spacing.
