et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and in each torch there should be one hole where the tumor is supposed to grow, and the torches should be firmly stuck in the ground so they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each pair of torches there should be a torch turning around the cord where the tumor is growing, and in each turning cord there should be two small torches an inch long to turn the tumor.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the cord that is between the torches to the tumor towards the head, and the other cord to the other torch towards the feet; and each of the assistants turn their respective torch so that the whole cord turns, and the master places the thorn even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is evened out, put on a desiccating plaster with abundance of egg, and then bandage, and then sewn up with the needle of a tablet of III deniers in length, that the place of the joint and the part of the spine may be properly aligned and the sinew healed; and tie it up with a cord, as we have said, and use gentle soothing treatment on the patient until they are cured.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if nothing comes to an end in the cure, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medications, with the needle that we have said before;
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and whenever one administers a splint, and the appearance comes to the back part of the spine near the back, and it seems that this is a dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that opens, for which reason one should not have any presumption:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	Perhaps it would bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	It seems we've reached the end of the text.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder do not get dislocations except alone, nor does it come from them in such a way as other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inside and outside, and in front and behind;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and further inside then that, and it is dislocated more forward than backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when you join the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased knee swells more than the healthy one, and the diseased person cannot fold their knee back.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the place that is near to the swelling of a hot abscess, because the head of the hip comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one to whom it happens outward is that this accident is contrary to those in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of him whose condition is ahead are that his leg feels well according to its completion.
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	Anyway, do not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him go, he cannot move forward, and holds his urine, and becomes inflamed with anger, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of the one to whom it happens in back are that he cannot stretch his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the groin is softened, and the veins of the thigh are at the level of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The returns of this likeness of dislocation are that you return to the place where the dislocation was ancient and it remains according to its position, then there is no cure.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it does not become necessary for him to have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in that whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four manners of dislocation, you should hasten to turn the joint inward and outward, and move it to the right and left.
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	perhaps he will recover, and there is no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, you must send the patient to a skilled minister, and have him lie down with his leg strongly grasped by two hands, or with a cloth tied above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and another minister extends his hand thus over him in such a manner that he pushes his hands under his buttocks, then tightens it with a thin strap above the thigh.
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another ties his head with the string;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and extend it upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four appearances, and if the dislocation has recovered, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, you must apply treatment to its likeness.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the hip, you must bind the patient on his healthy side, then put the strap over the root of the thigh, and the place which is under the groin, then pull the strap upwards towards the groin, and towards the femoral region.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	Then take some other servants with you, and embrace the large part of the sick person's thigh, and stretch it out fully at the back.
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it will come back to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot press it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft string on the two heels and on the two shins, and the sick leg be stretched out two fingers more than the others.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then it will be hung up on the top of a beam, and there will be over the earth two arms that are long;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then command the servant to embrace the head of the thigh, and there should be another servant hanging with the patient, who will tightly grasp the thigh, because the joint returns now hastily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at the farthest point, if the patient lies down, as we have said in the case of a clubfoot, and stretches it properly over the sick leg and also on the chest;
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two torches, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert the torch between the thighs of the patient in the form;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have plants of damp rushes surrounding him so that he does not hurt the patient, then stretch out each attendant towards him, and the surgeon places his hand equal to the dislocation on the patient's hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the table and press him thus as we have said in the joint setting, and position the patient on his sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch out the sick leg hastily, and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and the surgeon puts his hand on top of the swollen part of the sick leg, then presses with the other hand, and stretches it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is in front, it does not need to stretch the patient down, nor lift them up towards the earth, but rather they should be as if the back were dislocated in front, as we have said about lying on two backs;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and be on their face, and the string should be stretched as we have said before this, and one must press down on the joint at the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be straight when the patient stretches their legs, and they will be even;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then adjust the hips, and apply the splint, and bind with a bandage, so that the back does not move;
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and they should rest for three days or four, then release it, and apply the splint on top;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, then bind them, just as before, and leave for three days;
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then loosen it, and make it go gently, so long as the member is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	This is a continuation of the medieval medical text I was translating earlier.
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The jawbone is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inward and outward, and backward.
et ne desalue point devant.	and it does not get dislocated forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are such that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at their knee, and if it does not straighten out at their knee, then you know they are dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all such is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if they can, and place your back over their face, and put their foot on yours.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take their knee with your palms, and pull it between your teeth, then bend the two sides of the knee firmly.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another servant extends their foot, so long as the jawbone returns to its place, and the signs are that it straightens out at their knee lightly.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	And apply the poultice above, and make the leg warm to the knee, and bandage them together tightly for three days or four, then loosen it.
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and the patient should not be worked until the members are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not aligned, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	It seems like you're switching to a different medical condition.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The toes are sometimes swollen, and sometimes dislocated completely, inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tense before the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the return is light, and the joint should be stretched lightly with one's hands when it is moved alone.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated from the whole, then you should have the patient sit up straight, and tie one of his hands by the leg, above the ankle.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot to you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it up, and push the foot strongly upwards.
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this two times, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot.
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it goes back, that's good.
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and if not, repeat the work, because it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return thus, then have the patient lay on his back on the ground, and insert the splint firmly into the earth between his thighs, and tie cloths around, so that he does not injure the patient.

puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then extend each surgeon equally, and the splints should then be between the thighs of the patient to hold the patient when it is being extended.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then put the men on either side of the dislocation into their hands, and another surgeon will stretch the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it has hardened, put on the plaster and bandage over it, and shape the splint, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves which are above the ankle behind, so that the ligature is not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	then let it be for two or three days, and if the bandage loosens, reshape the splint.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then loosen it on the fourth day or quarter of that, and keep the patient from going for four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes before that term has ended, it is not sure that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are swellings on the feet that come, you should soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	It seems like you want me to say something about the text being from the "Traité sur les maladies de la peau" by Guy de Chauliac (also known as De chirurgia), a medieval medical treatise, specifically the section on treating foot injuries or dislocations. Is that correct?
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hands are dislocated, you should stretch them gently without working, and it's a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any way out of the back part of the foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a smooth plane or on .ie. table entirely straight, and put your foot on what shows of these joints, then press firmly with your foot until it sets.

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	It seems like you're grouping together the sections from the medieval medical text that deal with both wounds and dislocations of the feet. This section appears to be part of a larger treatise on treating injuries, specifically those affecting the hands (dos) and feet.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times has happened that the patient dies;
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not confident in the cure, since you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, nor too bold;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and start with soothing things to calm the abscess and let the patient be in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then reset the member to its place, so that the hot abscess may come;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, administer warm poultices to an abscess and cure the wound as it seems fitting with drying ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if with the dislocation there is fracture and small bones broken, take out the bones and do what we have said in simple illnesses.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and beware of entering into a path of fear, as I have said, for it is worth more to you than all the riches in the world, and for the knowledge that will arm and protect your body.
